O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, dear children, I have completed this book which is the culmination of the study of medicine combined with its full implementation, and brought to completion through its demonstrations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to my mind that I should complete this manual with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the manual work is widespread in our region and has been taken far and wide everywhere, it has lost its knowledge and expertise, and nothing remains from it beyond small descriptions in old books that were done by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this error and vanity, minds are closed off and the knowledge is far away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems I should revitalize this treatise in its entirety according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and will come together with the forms of the cautery instruments and other tools of work along with their proper exposition and preparation as required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And due to the reason that no good masters of hands are found in our times, the art of medicine has been prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that whoever intervenes promptly in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the disposition of the limbs, their forms and connections and separations, have knowledge of the bones and nerves and sinews, and the number of bones, and their movement and of moving veins and resting ones, and the location of their exit.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus states Hippocrates that with words we speak little and with deeds even less; indeed, in the art of manual skills.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever does not know what has been said beforehand, is likely to commit errors and deceive people; similarly, I have seen many who interfere in this science and abandon their knowledge and lack of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	And I have seen a fool who attempted to remove an abscess or neck swelling in a woman, and cut the arteries below the neck; because so much blood flowed out that the woman died from her hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I have seen another fool who treated a stone in an elderly man, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died after three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to extract it, and saw the location of the disease and the size of the stone, and if you had cut him, he would have died.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where he treated someone who was in need of care, Duke of our land, who had broken his leg and suffered bruising. The injuries were incorrectly applied to the wound causing unnecessary harm, and the patient was left with pain for an entire month; he was advised not to relieve himself at all during that period; so he remained like this until the leg swelled completely and the feet became infected, leading to death.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was summoned to assist him, and I hurried to relieve his leg. And when I heard that it had been released so smoothly without any pain being felt.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every path of corruption had already been confirmed in the member or body, and it could not be cured; and the process of decay continued within the member as long as the limb was completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And there is a second site that collapses an incised abscess and then inflames it due to the wickedness of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For the ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it does not permit one to touch it with iron if it is in such a state that all can be removed which is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And concerning this, dear children, you must know that work of the hands is divided into two sections: that is to say, where there are dangers in multiple conditions; and I will show in each part of this book where there is danger and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary that you keep them, so that the simple people do not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your weapons in caution, and treat your illnesses lightly yet firmly, and use the best way so that through God's grace you come to health and are healed; and leave the unbearable diseases with grievous sanitation; and remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in them so that you can come from this world to glory in the next.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen instructs in some of his admonishments: "Do not take ill disease as treatment, lest you be called a foolish person by others."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters deal with fire cauterizations and medical cauterizations, and organize the chapters from the head down to the stones; and about the forms of instruments, and tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in the operation.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, as well as suction cups and wounds, the extraction of arrows, and similar matters; and these chapters are organized along with the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, as well as similar matters; they are organized from the head down to the stones, and include the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we recall our work, it is fitting for me to tell you the quality of each remedy and its harm for every constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of assistance and damage are the longest speech and most subtle science and secrets in response. And many wise ones spoke about this, agreeing with it. They provided me with little of their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire aid works universally on any constitution where there is matter, because there are two constitutions: these are known as warm constitution with matter and dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the warm and dry constitution combined with matter, they devised a plan and said that fire cautery is a great aid. And the other ones said otherwise: that fire cautery only works for illnesses originating from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and should not be treated with hot diseases by heat or drying; and it contradicts those who say otherwise that the cautery provides great help to hot and dry illnesses that come into the bodies of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every passage, do not interfere with it except that which has been proven, and which a long-time user knows the art of cautery, and the diversity of skin types in humans, and the dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the occurrences and extent over time; we have no fear for other skin types, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And make all the parts resemble and agree with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my children, that a fire cautery contains secrets of healing, and is more beneficial than a burning medical treatment.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes out only from the body that is burned, and does not harm another body if you don't name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	The burning medicines spread from one part of the body to another by removing the evil, causing diseases during treatment. And sometimes, they trouble the patient.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, due to its height and the goodness of its essence, does not create this effect if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experimentation and the length of my service and study in the art, and it is true about things. And for this, I apologize for the length of my words, for I do not wish to withhold from you the secret which lies in fire, and the quality of the work, how it removes diseases from bodies, as the philosopher says by demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they agreed upon when the cauterizations should be performed, and they prescribed times.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, because the evils arising from it occur by help of the fire; and likewise if the cauterizations are for necessary pains beyond and before which cannot wait until greater mischief befall to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think like the foolish ones do, child; for a disease cured by cauterization does not recover. And they say this in this manner; but it is not as they think, for cauterizations are only medicine that changes complexion and dries the fluids that cause pain, valued more than medicine due to their urgency of action and the virtue of its work and authority.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And the ability is that disease comes none other than according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness and its virtue; and they are gathered within him the excesses due to the acquisition of meats and similar things, if it is not cauterization given at this point or where there is little excess and moisture, such as cauterizations for pain, and similar things, and that kind of pain does not recur; but this happens seldom.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And no one understands why cautery is considered part of medicine at the end, and that can be seen; but they don't believe that cautery should follow medicine after all, but their understanding is false, and it considers cautery as part of medicine because when we administer methods of treatments in any illness and they do not work, then we administer our cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Thus clearly the cautery is part of medicine, not according to the understanding of the people who misunderstand it.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauteries are better than iron ones, and they mentioned this only due to the quality of gold and its high substance. They also stated that the metal parts of a cautery don't cause ulcers; however, this is not true as I have proven it myself and found that it can indeed occur in some people; and gold cauteries are better than iron ones, just like they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And still, when you heat the gold tool, you do not know it is heated by the color of the gold, and it is immediately cooled; and if you heat it too much; then put it on fire; and so there is enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use our iron cautery that we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Otherwise, I have ordered you to write this chapter up to the thumb, so that it is easier to find the vision.
dou cautere olivaire	with an olive stick
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	A fire cautery works for moisture and cold on the brain, and there are two of them which we do by reason of an illness called 'soda', and due to many humors descending from the head as sweat, and from ears, and through a multitude of dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially for all diseases originating from cold such as paralysis, soda [possibly meaning heatstroke or fever], apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient's body is cleansed by a dissolving medicine altering the head. Three or four times, according to how the qualities and the heat and the custom of the illness can bear it; then afterwards cleanse the head from the ill entity.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then hold it between your hands, and place his hands on a hot stone; afterwards put the root of your palm under the root of his nose between his two nostrils; and let where your fingers go bleed, then heat up the cautery called 'olivare', which has this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it at its natural position with ink, and while descending and restraining your hand gradually, pinch a little and then relax; then lift your hand alone, and check if you see the bone. If you do not see the bone, start using the cautery until you see the bone as I have instructed; afterwards take one part of honey, and apply soft cotton within, place it under the ink, and let it stay for three days; after that place a buttered poultice; leave it on until all scabbing has disappeared; then treat the wound with tetracycline ointment until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if they were told by the old ones, that the longer a wound stays open, the more it purges; and for this reason, movement helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they were told that we should leave the cautery on until part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burnt from the bone, and treat it afterwards.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And it is said that we should allow the cautery to remain there, and press so hard that we lift out of the bone as wide as a small ring that women put in their earrings because fluids can flow out from this place. And should we let the wound stay open for a long time; afterwards we must clean it and bandage it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of using the cautery do not seem to be good for everything, except in those where there is a flow of fear; and I think that I should leave them as they are. For the shoulders become weakened by continuous solutions from nature, as we have shown elsewhere on other limbs; and even when the shoulders are weak due to natural reasons, my first reaction to using cautery is more healing for me, and with this method I work together for health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	from the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the head comes chronic pain and lasts long, one must use the patient's remedies and pills that are called 'cochie', and treatments for clearing the head and ears and bandages; and if one applies the cautery as we have previously stated to it, it will not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the head of the patient is of strong nature, and not too cold; thus apply to it a little from this cautery as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you do the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and apply one cautery where the bone is called "vassel"; and apply another method for suction cups; and lift your hand so that you don't touch the bone: patients feel much more pain in this cautery than others, and I will speak about it elsewhere; and it should be known that the cautery on the horns should be gentler than the one used for the middle part of the head, and that has a certain form:
dou cautere dou chief	The use of a hot iron commands the patient to allow hair growth until it is long and even; and if it pricks at its base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in the shoulder part and the disease spreads up to the eye, and the head is purged with mild medications, and we have performed other treatments that I mentioned under the division of diseases, but none of this helps: therefore, I apply cautery according to two ways, namely through a medicine of fever and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine-based cautery involves taking a spoonful of oil, and using the peel and the re-cooked (a process akin to cooking in broth) for one or two times per joint. Then apply it onto the temple area where the pain is localized so you can place the spoonful of oil on top of the skin; once she's placed there, hold and tighten well and leave like that for 12 hours; then release and remove the garlic paste, leaving the wound in that state for two days or three. Then apply a butter bandage until sweating appears.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the application of ointment until it is clean; and if you see that applying some burning medicines, as I have written or detailed in the second part on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is done like this. Heat up the shape of the cautery as described:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "closed" because its tip is shaped like a bell or has .i. point of curvature, and in the middle there's a small appearance; and put it on the painful area, and hold your hand and gently twist the iron until half of the edge of the wound is burned; then lift your hand so that no artery burns, let blood flow abundantly.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After placing sailcloth in the wound area and keeping it for three days; then replace with damp cotton in butter, and treat the wound with ointment until it is clean; and if you wish to cauterize this headache using the iron cautery which is called "cultellare", do so all over but be careful not to cover the artery in this headache that isn't old.
de emigraine	Of the migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraines as we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases before, and if it doesn't improve, and you observe that the cauterization methods previously discussed in medicine don't work on this individual either, then it is necessary for you to heat up the cauterizer called "cultellare" until it turns white; and do so by placing its tip half a line of about two inches along the spine, and take your hand once, and apply pressure ensuring not to touch an artery or cut until you reach bone; and be cautious with the jaw when one eats, making sure no food is left in it which could lead to choking, and that nothing else besides the silence occurs in the throat, avoiding any spasms that might affect the patient, and guard against bleeding from the artery once cut, or when you experience excessive fear about it, especially those who are not familiar with these procedures; just let me finish my work here for now; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and show you its location in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you notice that these cauterizations do not help the disease and the patient is suffering, apply cauterization to the middle of the head as we have said before, and treat the wound until it heals. And if you observe this, administer the cauterizer we mentioned in the chapter on extracting an artery, along with a double-edged cauterizer; and these are better than others and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of the ear from part frost.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When frosty pain strikes the ear, and remedies have been applied along with other treatments we've discussed in this section, should the pain persist, then apply a heat cautery known as "pains," as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez. de la torture de la bouche	From the pain of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Pain that should be treated with a cautery isn't removed by those that move due to lymph flow, just like we mentioned in the sections of diseases; and there shouldn't be any cautery for symptoms that come from dryness and irritation of the nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this form of pain that moves due to lymph flow and head discharges and gargling, and it doesn't respond well, then it's necessary for you to apply the cautery at three points: one at the root of the ear, and another slightly outside the temple, and the third in adjusting the two lips; and place the cautery over the healthy part that is exposed, and make it cauterize the area above the ear a bit below the head keratin layer, and another on the temple to the length of about an inch; and leave the cautery there until half the brain is burned; and this is how you should apply the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the form of cuteria we placed earlier, but it's a bit more refined and requires that the knives be slightly thicker; after treating the wound as I said previously until it heals properly, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with an apoplectic stroke that is long-lasting and you treat it as we have said, and if it doesn't improve, and the patient has a fever, then do this: make four cauterizations. Two of them on the two horns of the head, and one under the head, and one where the neck is called 'wattles' as we had previously mentioned, and the final cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it accordingly as we had said before.
de litargie	from Liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, you should give the patient large grains and powdered pills that purify the brain; afterwards take the scalp of the patient thoroughly, and place the sinapic plaster on the back of their head as written or described in treatments for plasters. And this is how to do the cautery: do it like I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is clean like this, well and good; and if not, proceed as follows: make three cautery burns descending from the head to the collarbone, leaving a space of about one finger between each burn. Treat as you would with other cases; should you see them adjusting and the patient tolerating the pain, perform another burn in the middle area. If necessary, do two more on the tips of the remaining two parts, treating until it is clean; among these burns, call those performed in the middle 'olive-shaped' like I've mentioned before.
de la froidor dou chief	of cold from the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit. de l’epilempsie	From the treatment of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine. Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	And if the patient is a child, then do one delicate cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to the reason of melancholy are excesses or fluids corrupted and thick, then apply the fire cautery from parts as we have said for the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division. After having the head of the flesh; after make two pieces of linen well made, as one circle, if you place it on the head; and if there are maladies sitting still, they should be held in all directions; afterwards present the liniment, and warm with old goat butter; and heat it over fire at a moderate temperature so that it can be applied without causing discomfort; after drain out the circle through from within by keeping the head covered, and let it cool down; and do this to each part of the body once per week with good governance until it is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you see that the cautery is being applied by making several points on the entire cautery. This method of cautering moistens the head significantly; and then place wet cotton, butter, and gelatine fat on it.
de l’awe des eulz	from the power of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the onset comes first with the eyes through the signs I have mentioned in the division, then begin and continue to make the patient consume something that purifies the head, and protects it from all moisture, and make him sweat or take multiple baths while fasting.

dou cors des larmes	of the two paths of tears

dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the paths of tears within the eyes

Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the oil paper is softened due to illness and moisture, then apply the cautery that is called 'olive'. Here is its form:

And if you see that they do this twice on the two candles as long as the candle is, and don't let go of your hand until the third part of the paper burns, according to the method I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that sticks out from the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has it been that the hair of the eyes turns into the gums and touches the eye, and then one performs a cautery according to two methods: namely by fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let their hair grow long and evenly; and if they are grasped at their root, hold their eyelids so that they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are even, then set the patient in a state of health; after this on the paper by which there is an eye, draw a figure that shall be as if it were a leaf of myrtle, and mark its beginning by the sign before the hairs; then place wet cotton saturated with quail's egg white and garlic paste over the eye, then warm up the cautery to the shape indicated here.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing at the figure you have marked little by little a few times, until the scars are healed in that place; and the signs of health after the operation is when you see the paper retracting, and the hairs raised to the eye point's level; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then put wet cotton in butter as long as the scorching disappears; afterwards apply an ointment until it becomes healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And when this comes about and the paper softens, then restart the cautery at that same spot as before; if the hairs have fallen out, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level and evenly matches, not touching the eyes.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of medical fire commands the patient to let their hairs grow long and even; then shape parchment like a leaf of myrtle. Then take French soap and fresh vinegar, each one part, mix them well; do this quickly so it doesn't cool off, then spread on the form as like a leaf of myrtle, put on paper over the eyes; if the patient is sick for less than an oil (unit), they should open in one place, and if both sides are similarly affected. And fill each hole with moist cotton from an egg; keep your hand on the sick person's body while spreading the medicine, press once every time the patient feels the irritation of the medicine, as it feels like fire also.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, if you apply the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the irritation has passed, if you lift your hand away, and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted as it would be lifted by constraining fire or through incision; and if this is so, then it is well. If not, reapply the medicine to your finger or where the medicine hasn't worked yet, until your actions are even, and your eyes are ready; then place moistened cotton in butter until the skin burns under them, after that cleanse your hand with balm which is called 'dyafenis' and another, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz. And if the paper becomes moist afterwards, and the hair grips in the eye, then restart the medicine on that side of the head which was softened by the proper paper; just as you did before; after it heals until it is sound; and this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	Know that the eyes of people are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and do not let the right way respond to him who is studying this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	by the treatment of fistula via cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat fistulas as we have instructed under the divisions of diseases, and your treatments are not benefiting, then it is necessary that you apply a cautery in this manner to them.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your healthy position; and guide the surgeons' hands on their head so that it does not move or shift from its position under your guidance; after this apply moist cotton in preparation for an egg or garlic juice onto the eye; then heat up the cautery which is prepared: and hold the heated cautery above the head as if it were a feather pen, assembled to be placed on the skin where it will touch. If you can see that its tip moves from one corner of the head to the other, or if you observe that it resembles an umbrella; but in any case, remember this procedure is crucial for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing if the fistula has been opened, and treat the infection by drying it out; and if it is closed, open it again and remove any pus. Afterwards, place the cautery in order, hold your hand on the cautery at the part near the nose above the eye, ensuring your hands do not cause chaos; then insert the cautery into the oil's grease, and let it become impure.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery until the bone, that would be well. If not, retry the cautery one more time and if needed, do so again, and let it rest for three days; afterwards apply moist cotton in butter, and continue with the drying ointment cure until it heals completely. If forty days have passed and it is still not healed, then apply a corrosive water medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow this procedure according to what would be recommended in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a way of cauterizing fistulas that none of the old ones mentioned. Understand what a fistula is, and prepare to treat it; afterwards place one sharp needle in the opening, following its natural shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And do it to the size of three inches of wood; and hold your hand or needle firmly, and don't move the body at all, so that the heated wood doesn't sear its oil; and one must put on the oil of the body cotton moistened with egg white or ash: The wood is the source of the fistula, and the body enjoys marvellous healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is cured by the cautery we have mentioned, that's good. If not, it should be treated with mercury, and bring back the fistula to the body according to what's proper in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	cuts in lips

de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the lymph node, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it turns into gangrene and swells up until it hardens and becomes a fistula; you then treat it as we have explained in divisions, but if this treatment doesn't help: then it's necessary that you use one fire cautery according to the size of the fistula; after draining or removing pus from the fistula, hold your hand until the heat penetrates to the bottom of it and wherever else is affected. And do this once or twice, as we have said in treatments, while it remains healthy. dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth

When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat this with medicines but it doesn't help, then place the patient's head in a healthy position; afterwards heat up the cautery according to its form which will come after this in such a manner that you insert one piece of wood into the tooth; and put within the cautery hot for a short time, hold your hand so much that the pain feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; afterward lift your hand and continue the cautery as you desire it; afterward fill the patient's mouth with salted water, leave it there for an hour and then rinse it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the moving tooth is stabilized, and the softened gum is restrained, and the moisture is corrupted and dried.
de la dolor des dens	from the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain comes from coldness, or there is coldness or veins involved, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it needs to use cautery according to two methods: and butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery if it is such that you take butter from a cow, and the tip in a metal spoon or spider; afterwards take cotton and wrap around the tip of a needle, and let the butter melt, then place this butter against the painful tooth quickly and hold until it has cooled down; do so repeatedly as long as its power reaches to the root of the tooth. And if you see wet wool and cotton in cold butter, and place them against the painful tooth, and place on a hot iron until the heat reaches the nerve of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	Fire cauteries if it is such that you take a piece of iron or spider, and make sure it is large enough so that the fire doesn't reach inside the wound; after heating the cautery, from which heat will come afterwards, place them against the tooth and hold your hand until the heat of the cautery has cooled down; do this repeatedly, as the pain will be gone by today or tomorrow. And make sure the wound fills with good butter when you hurry with the application of this cautery, and then remove it with force; this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cautery of whatever size you desire, and according to what you have the capability for; this is the form of the rod:
des scrophules	Of the scrofulas
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are caused by cold pus and moisture, and do not respond to digestive remedies, then prepare the cautery as described below, and make two openings for fumes to exit on the other side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery against the boil once or twice, or three times until it reaches the bottom of the boil; and if the boil is small, adjust the size of the cautery according to the size of the boil, and leave it like that for three days; and cover with moist cotton dipped in butter until the pus is removed; afterwards treat with oils and poultices until it heals.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cautery made from rue

de la menoison	from memory
