When you treat the "thehlul" condition, if it appears as a rough area, and you apply the fire cautery that seems like a razor's edge, then set it fully ablaze over that "thehlul" treated spot; and keep your hand there until the flame reaches the base of the vein from which the blood flows; perform this once or twice, and if there is more "thehlul", cauterize each part as we have said; after the treatment with antiseptic ointments when they are effective; and if you cauterize with a large fire cautery over "alchatim", it will provide greater relief.
de plaie mal curee	Of improperly treated wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot bear surgery or incision, as we will describe in its proper place, if such sickness occurs that can only be cured through cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there's a fistula that has aged and developed into gangrene due to moist infections, you should test the entire area with a thin needle, and remember to know exactly how many points the fistula penetrates. Heat the cautery to resemble the size of a small knife, then insert it into the fistula according to its depth, and reheat until the pus and decayed materials are burned away, one time, or two times, or three times depending on your need; be cautious not to burn nerves and major veins. If the fistula extends into the abdominal cavity or intestine, handle them with care, performing the procedure only inside the abdomen, consider that it's not a minor operation. After healing the area thoroughly until it is clean, if the wound has healed over and the contents have been digested for a long time, you can determine that the wound has fully healed; otherwise, know that there are still infections present in the fistula, decayed bone at its base; do this with understanding as we will explain further within its context.
de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain in the stomach comes from the kidneys and large congestion, it affects women differently, hence you should apply a cautery on both sides of the kidneys with the same cautery we mentioned before; and if we cauterize at the midpoint, there will be three cauterizations in line, and they will provide more assistance.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is full and weak due to heat and moisture so that the patient retains urine, then the practitioner should perform a cautery procedure on the lower part of the bladder, where hair begins near the thumb. On both right and left sides, each cautery should be as long as the span of one's hand; and apply a single cautery behind the back, or two if needed; and make sure the cauteries are in the shape described beforehand.
de la marris	Of the liver
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the liver is cold and moist, and fails to allow conception to occur, and the flowers (likely referring to some medical condition or symptoms) are putrefied with their ends delayed; and when they come in, there is much pain: then it's necessary to perform three cauterizations inside the womb, just as we have said about the cautery for the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and make sure the cauterizations are made in the shape of a claw, as we have said.
de la hainche	From the thigh
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous fluids descend to the crotch area of the thigh, and because of this reason it moves out of its place. The signs are that the leg is longer than the other when measured together; and the limbs are found from the division visible point, then you should cauterize the diseased part on the crotch area of the thigh with one fire cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the limb inside the crotch so that the crotch be within the circle; and let the cauteries be as those used for cauterizing the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have these fire cauteries ready, make three olive-sized fire cauteries instead, and ensure that the cauteries are as large as all your nails; and treat with them until they cool down.
de la dolor de la hainche	Regarding the pain in the thigh
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the thigh bone, and this is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated using what we have discussed about treatment for joint disorders, but the cure does not work, and the disease is old: thus, it is necessary that you cleanse the body of its large fluids with putrid pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu. Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche .iij. cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a .iiij. selonc ceste forme:	After you do the cautery; and the method of doing the cautery is according to two ways: this means combining hot medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is done in several ways; among which one method is as follows: you apply triangular cauterizations on the thigh bone in this shape, and each one should have good depth and be large, with an interval of about a coin between each one, and these cauterizations are olive-shaped; no one makes a middle cauterization in the middle part of the thigh because there are four according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that it is cauterized with the circular cautery as we have explained before in the dislocation of the thigh bone; but make it like this so that the circles contain all the thigh bone, and all the points around the wound are heated.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe. Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai .ij. cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et .i. cautere desus la cheville .iiij. dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor .iij. poins ou .iiij. au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And this is the method for sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and doesn't reach up to the thigh or down to the leg. And if it does come up to the thigh and the leg, they do two cauterizations there where the disease says the pain stays, and one on top of the ankle three inches, at the left side a bit; and be the cauterizations cutaneous, and burn the thickness of the skin; and if the patient senses that the pain extends up to three or four inches deep in the body or almost up to the knee, then they cauterize where they feel the pain.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if more work is required, do it; and should the pain extend from the knee towards the thigh, use cutaneous or circular cauterization, and take great care in all your cauterizations to not let off until you burn both nerves and major arteries, and make no greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who performed cauterization on the ankle down to the foot, and left them until their leg was completely swollen, and even so with the feet, which became inflamed and rotten. After an abdomen treatment, he/she died from it.
Et se li dolors est en .ij. parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere. // Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai .i. tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de .ij. pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait .i. mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the pains are in two parts together, do the cautery on each part according to this way. // And the surgeons said for the fire cautery of the hip, as stated here is the method, make one rod of iron and let it be at the head also as thick as a small carpenter's auger or slightly less, and have it with interstices and let them extend from one to another of space equal to the size of a button; and may the interstices be above the two parts and are like knots, and each has a well-made iron hand and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it becomes entirely toasty red and you smell scents emanating from it, and then place it on the sore area of the hip wound, and rotate it over the healthy side. And apply this cautery once with one piece of iron, leave it for three days; and afterwards cover it in butter, and let the wound remain open long enough; after the ointment treatment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we use a little of this cautery for the fear caused by its application, and we see few who use it; however, all the same, this is good cautery which one can endure, and allows where it happens.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by fall or from percussion or due to too much evacuation, or through indications of spread of cold matter, none of these appearances warrant cauterization. For it is the one who comes from the infusion of cold matter that deserves cautery.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary that after the body has been emptied of fetid pills or other indications, one performs this on the back where the pain occurs, three lines marked with a cross, and in each line according to the virtue and quantity the body can endure, more than .v. cauterizations; and do the cauterizations according to the cautery called "points"; and if you see fit, perform 3 or 4 cauterizations at the mid clavicle according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often befalls small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they feel tightness alone when they stand up and faint; and you find in the last spine at the back and upon us the appearance that comes to other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this [condition] and observe its cure, if you treat it with the fire cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument. Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant .ij. lignes ou .iij., et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	If you see this [condition] and observe its treatment, apply the reddish hot point to each part of the spine equally. And if you see that needs treatment, sear inside the spine with a sharp cautery for two or three lines, and have the points close together. After this, let it heal until it is clean according to what we have said, and be careful not to use the cautery in an area of gilbositeit which is near nerve damage.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain in joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain in joints is due to moisture that spreads throughout each limb, and when pain comes from inside the foot, which they call "gout" properly, and when it's caused by cold and needs medicine to cure it, then it can be treated using cautery in this way: make the shape of the cautery inside the joint of the foot, and apply olive oil to the cautery according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point». Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you need to touch the face near the foot, then apply heat over the entire area with this cautery. And if pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens frequently, then apply heat on each knee three times or four from each part, all across the olive oil heated area; and if you need more, make more but do not let your hand stray beyond until the inner warmth is burned out completely.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre. Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile .ij. lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines. Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, then apply the cautery as we have said in our chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, then make points inside the armpit two lines deep; and if there is no pain left on the back, then apply heat over each joint and the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up to elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and well govern your patient and provide medicine. For if you govern him well and purge phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	regarding the rupture of the scrotum
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture happens in anger, and the bowels descend into intestines it's new, so it must be that when you see him being cured, he does not consume anything that day; and he should use things that lighten his stomach, so that his innards descend from his stomach; after have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to shave off his armpit hair until the intestines are repaired, then pull them with your fingers, and scrape over the rupture on the bone of the finger, and at every sign it should resemble half a circle above the chest; then warm up the cautery as described here:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui .i. cussin et .i. serjant sus les cuisses, et .i. autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Until it is white and releases scents. Then pull the intestines by their ends; and have his servants shave off his hand so they do not turn back; and work well on his thighs with the patient, and place one cloth on his thighs and another under his buttocks, and another at his anus who shaves his hands; then put the cautery over his sign on your entire hand, and keep one straight and one bent until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again once more until you come to the bone; and take care to ensure that intestines do not spill when you apply heat; that you do not burn him; and that in this way, the patient does not suffer or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien. Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés .iij. jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides .xl. jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	Know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your works are useless. And it must be that children's cautery irons are subtle according to their size and large people's also large according to their measure; after three days, wash his abdomen with butter oil until the scab is removed; afterwards, apply other ointments until he feels well, and let him rest on his back for forty days until the wound heals properly; and it must be that his bedwetting becomes exhausted for a long time, so that intestines do not spill when he wants to go to chambers.
Et aprés .xl. jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse .xl. autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement. Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, a well-made bandage should be placed on him and worn for forty more days; with good rest, he must work little and guard against excessive drinking and eating, and loud shouting; and once this instruction is followed thoroughly, he will be completely healed. And I shall speak of the treatment of tailing in my chapter afterward.
de la routure dou ventre	regarding the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai .j. cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a .iij. angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you notice that they no longer grow, then with each of those ruptures apply fire according to its quantity; let it be three parts of the cup's measure for the third one after each cure following what we have said; and none of the elders have said that one should cauterize at the cautery at three angles according to this form:

de dolor anciene en aucun membre	from old pain in no limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any limb, whether from falling or being hit, and if this pain lasts long, and the cure of medicine doesn't help, then it should be treated with a cautery known as 'poins', and the cauterizations should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its function and location of twists and pain. If the first application of heat is effective, that's good; if not, apply another one on top of it, for such things are accustomed to move towards the body part closest to them, so you must do the cauterizations until the disease has healed.
de meselerie	Of cautery with fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai .v. cauteres sus lou chief: .i. emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et .ij. sus les .ij. cornes, et .i. derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	The treatments for cautery involve many times and with great assistance, and similarly the disease that comes from the putrefaction of bile and melancholy. If you see them being cauterized, take care when this disease is in its beginning phase, and if it's cured according to what we have said in division, and doesn't recur or stay, then doubt that corruption spreads through the entire body, so do this: give five applications for cautery: one on the head at noon, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the cheekbones; and let your hand be such that the heat of the cautery reaches up to the bone, and so much that the crusts come out forcibly so as for the vapors of thick humors could emerge; and cauterize also under the skin according to what was explained earlier.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the meseil is everywhere spread out; and it becomes apparent that you should cauterize with these cauteries we have said about earlier: on the head, and one cauterization in the nose area, and two cauteries on the spine from neck to shoulder, and six on the spine of the back, and a large one under the chin and another at its center, and two on each shoulder blade; and two over the ribs, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one over each joint of hands and feet, and over the hollows of the hands; be careful not to burn any nerves that are behind the heel, do not burn them. And never make a cauterization above the bone under the nail, and another over the bone of stomach, and another over the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that the more I apply heat from a fire, the more assistance I give and benefit accrues; and know that patients do not feel pain during heat treatment as healthy people do, because their bodies are already completely corrupted. And it is necessary for the application of heat to be large and small according to limbs and joints, just like you will find in guidelines on using tools. After care, apply a mixture of flour with honey and other treatments until it is properly healed.
de enfleure	of inflation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When swelling appears in any part of the body and is treated with medicines, oils, and bandages, and does not heal properly, then I apply heat to the affected limb according to its size; and if the swelling comes through the veins, I perform cauteries on the limb. Then continue with treatments until it heals completely. And one should never do a cautery at the hand, foot, or back, where the nerves are found that can paralyze the limb, and thus remove the swelling in this way; and no one should interfere with this if they aren't familiar with limbs and the functions of moving body nerves.
de albaras	Of cautery with fire, command the sick person to let their hairs grow long and even; and if they poke at their root, hold their eyes still so they don't move until they fully grow.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the illness referred to as 'albaras' matures and medicine does not help, then cauterize using a small fire cautery according to the quantity of hair on the area. Do this until the boil is removed and its color changes; then cleanse with flour mixed with lentils, rose oil, and plantain leaves, along with colostrum and almond milk from each ingredient in equal parts. Mix all together, wrap with a cloth, and apply to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for the sore by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the ulcer begins to form and you observe it stop, if you want to cauterize it, use the fire cautery that seems like a half-circle, all around the circumference of the ulcer. And always some say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the ulcer; and always I do not think this is good because I fear it might lead to ulceration and corruption, and I have already decided never to do so; and more proper procedure would be to cauterize around, using the cautery called 'circule', as we mentioned earlier about types of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot die away
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is slow to die out, due to excess or because of the old age when it's decrepit (that means too old), and he has little blood left in his body, or because of tension; then you should observe for its hastening towards death. In that case, cauterize with small fire cauteries while holding them there; after this, leave him as is. For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through completely by the cautery, so heat the cautery as shown below:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of the illness that is called 'adubelati', while the cauteries have pierced through the whole body, and make these cauteries such that the patient feels them penetrate outwardly in such a way that the process of decay is alleviated. Afterward, proceed with the treatment until it has been fully healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire using iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of illness is called 'corrodens', which is simply a diseased member, causing it to burn like dried wood. If you see this disease in someone who can withstand the iron cautery together with fire, then heat the cauteries slightly and large according to what suits the body or where the disease is; after that, cauterize around all parts until you remove all corruption, leaving nothing behind, so that everything that has been corrupted is removed. And leave it for three days, then apply burning with oil to those cauterized areas as long as the burns from the fire heal and eliminate all corruption. After this treatment using remedies that produce pus.  And if you see after three days that healthy skin doesn't emerge, it's good; but if not, then start cauterizing in the same area that has remained of the corrupted flesh. This diseased condition can often be treated with medicine from water instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is a greater aid, and I have already mentioned the treatment for water remedies under its division: take it as needed when you have it available.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	From those who come to the stones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Not many times when stones produce a disease which we call "cyst" according to our understanding, and it is a large swelling that presses on the foot. And for this disease there are two ways of treatment. These are known as fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery involves heating up one iron rod like a feather from a rooster, and it should be made of good iron at a size that it can fit around any nail in all directions, and it should have thin margins; after this, place the heated rod completely on the nail, and twist your hand tightly around the rod until you reach the tip of the nail; then leave it like this for three days until pus starts to form. Then apply a plaster made from crushed wild garlic mixed with butter oil onto the area all night long, and the nail will come out along with its roots. Afterwards, treat the wound with anointing oil until it heals fully.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are inverted from within, causing disease in both the hand and foot, it is necessary that you apply a hot water cautery; and proceed as follows: take a hair stick or iron rod, or a rooster feather, and place it on the nail along with a small wormwood plant, this being for wart-like growths; then place the hair stick so that it touches all around, then add some hot water, hold your hand firmly in place, twist your hand back until the edge of the stick reaches to the root of the nail, and can find the deep passage of hot water down to the root; and let the patient endure a little bit of the hot water's irritation for an hour; then leave it like this, and all its roots will come out. Do this again repeatedly until you have removed all those that are in the flesh, then treat any ointments that produce pus.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake from cold or nerves, or from the quartan fever or other causes, it is fitting that you apply four or five cauterizations to the spine of the back. Apply one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the chest with an olive oil cautery; if this does not stop the shaking, hasten the recovery of the patient's health from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	The pus-sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	When pustules or sores become visible due to the exposure of the body or from large decayed matter, it is fitting that upon their appearance you apply a subtle fire cautery on each part of the pustule: a small stick of myrtle wood, which has its tip set alight with flame, or a long root of aristolochia, or an elliptical shape fire cauterizer. Never apply the cautery when they first appear, according to this manner, but rather it should remove the excess fluid causing them; and they become healed. But it is necessary that this be done after blood has been evacuated.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there occur great streams of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound when it flows outwards, or during incisions on an abscess, or with the cautery applied to limbs, and similar situations; it is much distressing to hear this.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to anyone, if you need to quickly place your index finger on the vein wound and apply pressure until the pain subsides under your finger, and no more drops leak out; then heat various small and large olive oil lamps until they are all red. Then take one (or adjust based on the size of the wound and the location of the artery), and position it over the vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery in place as long as the pain is relieved.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery is off the fire, then quickly take another one (.i., meaning 'one') of the cauterizing tools that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after another until the bone is broken; and be careful that you don't burn the nerve which lies beneath it, nor allow any harm to come upon the patient; and know that when the bone breaks from the artery, you may not properly set it by yourself even if the artery is large, unless done through one of four ways as we have said: by cautery, or extraction when it hasn't been treated yet, or with a strong hold on a thread, or through medicine placed upon it which has power to set blood; and then bind and restrain it immediately afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the setting of a fractured limb by tightly binding it with cloths or placing burning objects upon it, or other similar actions, if they do not benefit when done correctly.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have any sight or medicine nearby, then they should place their thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and stretch it well until the bone is set both over the wound and over the vein; and do not move the arm but keep it moist with cold water often until it becomes very cold, until the bone is frozen, swollen and set. And make incisions in front of what needs cautery or medicine treatment.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book of treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have explained in the first chapter all illnesses for which fire cautery or hot medicine is required, including the applications and causes, as well as the instruments and forms of cauterization. I ended that chapter at the knee joint, and now I will proceed through this chapter using the same approach because we find more easily what we want here.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this one, it is necessary for you, dear reader, to understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of cauterizations, so more caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the course of this chapter, there are often instances of blood evacuation when opening veins and incising abscesses, as well as treatment for wounds, extraction of arrows, cutting into stones, and similar matters; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I warn you not to embark on folly. For many ways of people come in cures. Some come from those who were so afflicted by their illness that they died lightly because of the madness they found in their disease, and the great suffering from their malice; and one should have fear towards these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And there are some who give you their insight and say: "Wait, I am skilled"; and the illness is deceitful. It would be inappropriate for you to consent to those who come seeking your help with this manner, but place more consideration in honoring yourself than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely of what you are certain of and can have; and use prediction and guidance in treating your ailments where health is converted; and this will assist you to acquire good reputation, glory, and long-lasting memory.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire from the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have instructed you this chapter by chapters, according to what is before or the section on cauterization, that I have outlined from head to feet, for you find it more easily of what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness comes very often to children at birth, and when the mother presses too hard on the head of the child; and it also happens sometimes due to reasons unknown.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never see this illness occur except in children, and among all those I have seen, their death came quickly; and because of that, it seems to me that it would be better for me to abandon the task of treating such illnesses partially.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw two infants of this condition, the shoulder was filled with water, and the head swelled each day until it couldn't bear it anymore; he believed in so much moisture that he died, and this moisture is assembled underneath the bone near the axilla, between the muscle and the bone. And the incisions are such that if there's moisture between the muscle and bone, and the abscesses are small, you cut through the head one wide slit; and it should be as long as two fingers, as long as the moisture flows; and see this form of the spathilium:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	And if there's more moisture, and the abscess is larger, make two cuts in a manner resembling a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is underneath the bone, and you see that the edges of the head open from each part, and water splashes when you press it with your hand on the inside, and this does not respond to your touch: then you must make three cuts in the middle of the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all moisture outside. After bandaging and powdering the cuts, apply wine and oil, letting it stay until the fifth day; then reset the position, treat the wound with bandages and ointments, let it heal properly, and finally give the patient dry meat of a small animal devoid of moisture as long as the limb is strong and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the opening of the abscess lies, and align with the water; for it never stands before; never behind; neither to the right; nor to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut therefore where the abscess opens, and where water fills it, and cut in accordance with what you can do; and be careful not to touch an artery; and watch for a flow of blood, so that the patient dies due to the release of blood and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of cautery treatment instructs to allow hair growth long and even; if they are sharp at their roots, hold tightly so they do not move until fully grown.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When any disease called 'catarrh' affects the eyes or anus, and it's an old ailment, and medical remedies don't help, then the last resort treatment is to use a cautery with cutting off of both arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you have to cut the eyes off, perform this treatment after removing its head; afterwards wipe out the area with a coarse cloth until the arteries are visible, then pull out the eye socket as far as two cloths. Then look where the vein is located, and compare both eyes from each side of their ears, and make sure they're properly set; then mark the eyes diagonally, then cut each one with an extremely sharp knife up to bone, ensuring it reaches all the way down to the bone.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, block the spur off of the artery and vein above, by cutting as well as two inches through.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is severed, make sure that the heart continues to pump blood upwards constantly outside.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open upon feeling it, you need to measure the length of about three inches, then cut until you reach the bone; and what needs to be removed of blood is about 7 cc, plus or minus depending on what the patient can endure, and the filling of the artery; then examine the wound: if there's still a point directly under the bone, or if no part of the abscess remains in place after removal, then you need to clean out the wound, apply bandages, and treat with ointments until it heals.
de emigrainne	Of the cautery treatment,
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old age comes and acute coughing occur, because of the moisture in tears and body heat around the temples and elsewhere for many years, it's a condition that can be treated with methods of medical cures and all this doesn't help. We extract veins from the temples and apply hot cauterization techniques as we have detailed.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The method of extracting them is such that the patient feels on their temple's hairs, and you can hear the artery emerging from the temple, for it opens well with its pulsation, and responds only in some people who are too cold; and if it does respond, you guide the patient using a strip of cloth, then rub their head against a rough cloth, and heat it up with hot water until the artery clearly appears. Then take the silver cup that's shaped as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then lightly remove the skin until you reach the artery, then guide it up with tongs and remove well the webs that are at each part; and if the artery is delicate, cut it at the tip of the claw. Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And guide the blood from seven cuts up to three; and if the artery is large, it's necessary that you tie it with two threads of a strong silk line for seven lengths, so that putrefaction doesn't occur in front of the welding of the wound, nor repeatedly bleed; then cut off the excess between those two threads at that moment. And then, if you see fit, apply the cautery gently up to the bone as long as the joints are covered; and this is the rough work, if the patient doesn't have fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterizations assist in finishing off moisture: for this is more assistance against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	When it comes to extracting arteries, one must fill the arm with old cotton and place well-made bandages on it; and when they are released, apply dry medicinal substances that produce pus and bandages until the wound heals. And if there's no artery bleeding, do your best with cautering tools or use the space filled with vitriol in your hand to ensure the wound is sealed; and if you don't have this on hand, place ice inside it until the bleeding stops, then rinse with cold water until the bleeding ceases, ensuring a proper seal. When the artery extracted is softer and lighter during extraction of the artery, you should cauterize the vein from that cautering tool cutting down two parts but ensure the cuts are well-spaced to preserve heat for longer periods.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the tools become too tight, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be about one finger's width between the two knives, and then when you have heated them up to touch bone, place the hot iron until it reaches the bone, cauterize the vein in two places; and keep them apart by a distance of about one finger for this cautery tool doesn't fuse completely throughout; and this is the shape of the cautery.
des larmes	Of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are flowing from veins that are above the test of the head's main part, and medicine treatments do not benefit, you see the face turn red, and feel or sense like trembles; and if they stay there moist such that the paper's hair falls, and the papers heat up, and burn due to the burning tears, it requires this treatment.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called the old one 'healing burn', and do this: tell the person with this illness to keep hair on their forehead, then make three cuts evenly across the forehead according to its length; and make one of the cuts like two marks all across the forehead downwards until it stops just above the nose, and the others two each over a rib by the papers, and be careful not to cut the arteries that run over the ribs by the papers; and keep your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and ensure each wound is about the size of three marks across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And prepare a piece of sponge and some cloths for it to soak up blood, then use the sharp tip from two parts in which this form is made:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made near the temple up to the second incision; and burn everything in the channel that is between the two gaps right up to the sinew which lies above the bone. si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Place the tool called a "cultellaire" in the first gap; it is very sharp on one side and blunt on the other, not sharp, and its shape is:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. And place the blade of the tool towards the airbone muscle in the tendon, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and push the tool until it reaches halfway through this incision. And remove all vessels that descend from the main artery to the veins up until the incision continues until the opening appears at the tendon, then continue this operation halfway down the first incision until the other gap; and then drain blood evenly, express the wound for the taken blood; then place a piece of old cotton in each gap, and cover with wrung out cloths soaked in wine and oil and garlic, and make sure no pus leaks out; and on the third day remove the stitches, and apply large amounts of vinegar compresses, then do the ointment cure of basil with oil rose, and other treatments used for wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of ear piercing
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	Everything that chokes in the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or animal, or mine stone or similar objects such as iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas; or flowing substances like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When it chokes in the ear a piece or some other object that doesn't fit into the ear or doesn't grow inside the ear, place the ear under the sun. If you can see the piece, apply a drop of violet oil or juniper oil, then proceed with extraction; and let them sneeze with consin, and stop up their nostrils when they sneeze, put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear, and elevate the ear above. This cure works many times; and if it does not work, apply extraction using small sharp forceps, as described here:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps as if under pressure, that's good; if not, proceed with the extraction using small, sharp tweezers; and if it doesn't jump like that, use an arachnid's claw and pinch the tip of the claw or the ear fur. And when you are at the part covered by wax, stick in a piece of beeswax so that the needle cannot enter with the claw; then press the forceps into place for forming, as often happens according to what we have said; and if it doesn't come out forcibly like that, take glut from one end and pinch its fleshy part, insert an instrument suitable for this task at one point, and put a bit of cotton in between; then press the glut onto the stone or anything else, and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't jump like that from all these things we've said, hurry to pierce the ear in such a way that pus and chalz come out with spasms; and the way of piercing is as follows: you make an incision first in the head vein, and remove blood according to its size. Then place the patient's hand between your hands and turn their ear up, and make a small cut at the base of the ear by the fat or what hangs down; and let the cut be like a crescent moon as you go towards the stone, then break the bone according to your ability, and suck it quickly into your mouth; and treat until it's clean.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it's grains that are inside and they swell, proceed with extraction; and if it cannot come out, use this small spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision on that grain. If not, take several stones according to their length and gently, then warm them slightly over fire; and place one or more of these on her ear, and remove from two parts of her feet, and perform another incision with a stone on the stone that's in the ear; and do not stop doing this stone by stone until all the water comes out entirely, and thus she discharges it all completely; and if you see, take one reed, and place one shoulder inside the ear, and the other shoulder over fire until the hotter end of the reed is burnt; then redo another part with more reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said about this stone.

And make it of silver or an animal ear narrow at the bottom to half a small spoon, and wide at the top for distillation; and in order to press within the distillation use one well-made tool from an animal ear suitable for this.
