de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the cauterization with fire,
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any remnants in their ears; and this very thing happens to people due to the pinching of wounds, or dead flesh within the ear canal, and these pinchings enter the ear on no account if one cannot see them; and not once does a single piece escape being seen by all.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which enters the ear and cannot be seen is due to pus in various dispositions, and you should understand that it is appropriate for you to place the ear of the patient towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the superficial pustulation, if the operation has completed this formation:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And indeed, and cutting in front and behind completely flatly so it doesn't hurt the ear; if the swelling is of a newborn or a part of the ear, if you have delicate pincers, gently scrape it off, until that bone is fully removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the swellings go inside the ear canal, take a fine rasp and lightly scrape it with heat, then insert into the part of the ear. If you feel the swelling that causes the skin to itch in the ear, pierce lightly, and ensure not to damage the ear's nerves; then insert a tent according to the width at its tip, and fill the ear with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and fill it with rose water and powdered vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, you should replace the tent and use another one filled with a wad made from rose oil and beeswax, until that swelling bone is removed; then continue to treat until it is clean.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, one dips an sponge and wraps it in cold water, placing it on the ear, and uses other treatments that help to stop the bleeding which are akin to those of distillation methods.
de la char des papieres	From the flesh of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	If the hairs come out in papers when they are moist and dry, it is necessary that you spread them with forceps and tweezers, and apply a poultice made from the roots of a spatumile; then place it on the affected area with vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it's not removed by peeling, cauterize with a thin lens cautery and then cauterization after incision is effective; and repeatedly apply, since nothing remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized by fire, those roots burn completely and do not return.
de la gresle	From the stone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times in papers there are things that seem like stones both in shape and hardness, and because of this, the disease is called 'hail', and it's a gathering of moisture being large on the paper above and below; the actions to take are: watch if hail moves from one side and another, and this is a light thing to know; do then widely, then burn each part lightly, then grab it with tweezers, and cover. If you can't cover without piercing a bit of the paper, or if it doesn't hurt anyone; and if the tear is large, if there's an opening in the gathering, treat until it heals; and if it's small, do not exert any force on it, for ointments restore it quickly and nurture flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if hail falls into the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and have hail at some tweezers, cover and press from both sides; and if the paper is moved away by the cut, it doesn't hurt anything; and when hail is covered, rinse with salty water, treat the area where flesh nourishes until the patient becomes healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	from the oil of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exina is an oil that gathers on the sheets of papers above, and this happens more often in children than in adults, causing much discomfort to their eyes. It comes as mucus in the morning, and they can't look at the sunlight because tears rush to their eyes; hence they lie down by their sides until noon, lying straight up, and have their papers damp beneath their brows due to Exina spreading into the eye. And when you press your finger on it with your thumbs, you feel the Exina going in between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of treatment is that when someone with Exina puts their head on a healthy place; and then take one linen cloth, and set up a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity of Exina contained by each part, then put it there; press your fingers from both sides so that all the Exina gathers inside the circle; then make a cut in the middle of the moist area diagonally, not wider than the wound you would make when opening a vein; and let the leather cover completely until you see the Exina through it; and multiple times the Exina comes out from the slit according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take it out then, in one piece, the thick cloth strip between your fingers at the front, and turn your hand right and left until it is spread; and be sure not to adjust in the crack, do not come to the whole pus-filled area up to the eye, do not prick it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it exits through the start of the crack, widen it gently slightly until it opens; then take it out as we have said, then moisten with a cloth and water, and place on the affected area, then remove by bending.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are any that grind meal and put it on to corrupt the moisture which remains. Then treat until it is well. And if pus comes out at the wound, then treat with restorative plasters until it is well.
des poilz des papieres	Of the hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs in an altered manner and they age, these affect the eyes and cause maladies such as habitual watering and paper yellowing and swelling, all of which are consequences of eye damage; and one treats according to four methods: or by applying a cautery together with fire, or with medicine according to what is mentioned before in the chapter on the cautery, and it's done either through incision and suturing or with bandages, depending on what I will explain.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary for you to place the eye's head in its healthy state, then turn the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it turns, that is good; if not, if you stick a needle with one thread on it at both ends. And do this either within the edge of the paper or beneath where the hairs grow from these altered hairs, and pull the thread across the entire length of the paper, then turn it using scissors. Then cut in the area under the paper, under the grown hairs, up to the root for the large tear all the way to the small one; then remove the thread, place a small cotton tent and lace over the paper, then on the paper make an engraving, like the leaf of myrtle, and remember that the design should correspond to the amount you see raised above the paper.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And when it comes to the part that requires one to use a large quantity of paper according to how soft the paper is; then do everything on top of the two lines you have indicated, and start with the largest hole until small. And there should be one of the cuts close to the natural hairs in the growth stage of a root, then pinch the thyme into one of the angles near the nose, then scrape all over it; then join the two lips together by one stitch on an ivory needle with one thread of fine wool and wipe away the blood. And do this process around the two corners with some sticky substances if you see fit; and should you not be able to perform this step correctly, don't worry about it, leave the stitches open until three or four days or five; then treat the wound without stitching with dry and constraining things since paper renews itself from the healing of the wound and the joining of them together. However, the stitches will dissolve (as said by the old ones), and this is work done without fear;
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there's another way: and you should mark the paper with a shape that is as like the leaf of thyme, as we have described it, cut out three inches according to the form shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then cut those that are above evenly with small forces according to the shape shown here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you cannot hold the forceps, and if the thing is not even, take one thread or has it two threads, and place the needle through its figure; then pull another thread from under the large sinew, and the second thread from under the small one, and assemble between your fingers the threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above which you have signed, as we have mentioned previously, then stitch together the two edges of the wound by suture, and treat it until it is healed; and if pus comes to your incision, soothe it with tallow and similar healing ointments.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And it often happens that the paper hair gets mixed up: so you should use what we have said about incisions; but the stitches in one and the other are more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the eyes follows this form: and you should invert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then create two canes by art, and two thin strings as long as the paper is wide; and shape each eye out of one half of the sheet; then carefully join them both together above the part of the paper that covers the eye, and stretch the two canes from each side in a formed manner; and leave it like this for several days, and the skin which has been stretched will shrink and harden and fit well, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it lingers, if the patient bears pain, then treat him until he becomes sane; and when the wound has healed, and when you lift the bandage, and no longer will hair grow; and this is the form of the two canines that you must follow in accordance with this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedures are as follows: you should take a delicate needle, and tie two pieces of fine silk thread together; then join the threads and skillfully knot them both finely. The length of each thread should be about a palm's width. Then place another short piece of fine silk thread in the chase and knot it at both ends. Next, place the patient's end on your healthy part; and when the light shines upon it so that you can see clearly, this is due to its subtlety and minuteness. Then insert the needle into the root of the hair where you've adjusted the silk thread, and pierce through the paper swiftly as you pull up from natural hair. Next, remove all hair until it is out of the chase along with the natural hair; then knot in the chase any remaining hair if there are two, three or more. Finally, remove your hand once the hair has come out of the chase together with the natural hair throughout.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase has been treated and no hair comes out with it, pull out the chase from underneath all the thread that you have ordered in place until the chase is removed beyond the tip and you can see this through your vision; then pull out the chase and thread, and apply oil to them for two or three days. Wait until the hair hardens in its place and the hair grows back; and if the hair is small, accompany it with one long strand of a natural cow's hair, raise it along with that or leave it hanging down until it becomes longer, then lift it up.
de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding the decay of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	For the illness which is called "aleacrati" or eye decay comes within the eye, if there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. And happens suddenly from a wound, or from a tailor's work or a cautery, and from similar matters.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the manner of this treatment for it is that you cut through that seam, and open up the eyelids, and insert linen strips inside, and hold them until they are healed; and you should not use things in its treatment which dry out or restrict. For if you do this, the illness will return worse than the first one; but work with softening substances, like fennel; and let water or decoctions of linseed oil be used, and linseed paste applied to it, and wrap a linen strip around it, and treat it in that way.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your treatment are that you must take care not to have it heal in a manner that conforms to its original form; and these treatments which we have mentioned here do nothing but address this illness, so that it does not recur according to its original form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	The material that comes to the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease which is truly called 'axacrati', and is natural and accidental. The accidents come from wounds, splits, cauterizations, and similar things; and the way of the operation in it like you pierce with a needle into the flesh, where there's two threads inside it. You insert them on the left tear duct until they are at the backside, so that the threads emerge through two cuts in the flesh; then the flesh goes above all over to cover the entire needle, and the paste forms around one large lump.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper figure returns according to what should be, it's good; but if not, take a needle and place it in the cut, then turn the paper and make two cuts inside the paper itself; and let the ends of the two cuts be at the corners of the incision that you made, so that when they are joined together, the figure looks like a letter which has no 'griesche' (a term used to describe a particular type of character or style); then remove this flesh according to its thickness until it's as much as was under the paper, following the one who placed the paper; then join the two cut-off parts and sew them with thread made of wool. Then perform the cure as we have said for medicines that soften, and with remedies, until it is healed completely.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or stitch or cautery, then it is necessary that you cut a full crease along the hairs of the papers, and according to what was said before; then cut between the two flaps of a tent, as I have said; and must do the work according to the shape of the disease, for she is very diverse in shape, and the surgeons prepare equipment everywhere so that they can know how to return the figure to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what it requires from work and tools in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	quickly of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this stitch occurs with people in such a way that the paper above is bound by the white of the egg, and cannot move or do its natural tasks, then it follows that you must pierce the corner of a pairer under the paper, and lift it up; and place it on tweezers, until you feel the fine spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too deep, so that the patient does not suffer from the sharp spatula cutting their eye or causing redness in the eye; make your incision, and burn this assembled part lightly, so that the paper heals according to its natural form; and it is cured throughout this whole thing, and do not put any salty water into the eye once, then take it out with cool water and a bandage; then place between the paper and the eye a linen tent, and cover the eye with wet wool; and after a few days use a colander and other tight things until it is fully healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	From the eyelid of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is in two ways: it is nervous and resembles one hard bone, and another which is not nervous, but resembles white moist congealed, that when touched with iron and cared for like with needle pricks, you cannot do; and both appearances begin near the major lacrimal duct, and grow slowly and slowly until it covers all of the eye and all light and movement of the eye.
