de la char sor le neis	from the flesh around the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	None of them are born or die from various knots, some of which seem like scorpions with the mouth of a pie. And if there is such a case where there's an attached knot of fuchsia color, and if there's a knot of good color, in that case, for these knots that are of good color and not attached, it is fitting that you place the patient between your hands facing the sun; and work their nostrils, and pour vinegar onto those knots, and force them out. Then collect what you can endure on the subtle sharp edge of one side until you know that that knot has been entirely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is any part that cannot be cured, when opening the entire body with small and gentle instruments, making sure nothing remains; and if without causing pain or forming pus, in case of abscesses, cut them according to need; and if it's malignant ulcers, quickly treat and cauterize until all pus has drained out, and all the wounds are healed; then let the patient bathe with cold water or use vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if it's the nose that's affected, and moisture reaches up to the palate, you should know it's infected; and if moisture doesn't reach as it should, there is new tissue forming in the bone above, so these tools are not able to cut properly: thus, it's necessary for you to insert one twine of linen slightly thick near each nostril, holding them with your fingers, keeping about an inch or less spacing between each knot; and place each patient under this linen thread while it comes out through their nose, pulling gently until the pus comes out from inside the mouth; and often children do this in school, and it's a simple task for someone who wishes to do so. Then hold the head that comes out by one hand and the other head that comes out by the mouth with the other hand, and know them one after another while you're holding our fingers together. Do this until you can tell that the pus has corrupted that tissue, then remove the threads, drain the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back under the nose as before; do this for three or more days, until the ointments have dissolved all the remaining flesh; and after that, place a cotton plug in the nose for some days until it heals, and if there's need for dried medicine use them; this is how the tool to purify the head works, which distills oils and medicines or wine.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And use silver or sulfur, resembling an open lamp like a stick, and guide it this way; and if you see the need, make a closed stick, and let these tools be full for purifying the head; and hold one part of the head when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh to the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease is born under the nose which is called "telul" and grows to become large until it can be seen; and for this reason you should cut at its beginning, remove all bone, then place the cautery or burning medicine there; and if you delay cutting until it becomes large, take care not to let it be hard, change color, lose sensation: do not touch it with iron as it's a trapped abscess; because once you cut it even once, it causes great mischief to the patient; and if the abscess is due to soft pressure rather than changing color, and you see that it can all be cut, let the patient bleed without fear, and treat the area with dried and restricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose is cut and stitched.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when a continuation of the venous blood comes into one of these veins, it benefits little, for not in all people. Therefore, let this happen to none if the wound is fresh throughout its blood; and then adjust the two lips to a stitch, afterward treat until it heals completely. And if the lips have become dry on both sides, it must be that you scorch all parts of their cure until they heal, then join the two lips to a stitch, and compress them, and dust with dragon's blood powder, and incense ground; and place the powders under a piece of plaster of great strength or another soldering plaster, and let it remain until it discharges by itself, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is as follows: you join the cut: either with needles, as we said in stomach stitch; or with thread, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	from the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the hands of the surgeon within the wound abscess firm, resembling grains sometimes, and smaller and larger; therefore it must be that you close the mouth, cut into each nodule, and take it with forceps and remove in each part; then use the hand after the vitriol incision until the pus is drained; and then drain the fluid quickly, and clean the wound from dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	from the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times it forms on the attached gum flesh, which the old ones called "albulus"; it must be held with forceps and cut at its root, allowing for bleeding or blood. Then place under the vitriol (sulphuric acid) or other drying and retarding powders; and if that flesh returns after incision, and many times happens, if it is cut a second time, then cauterize it: if it does not return after cauterization; these are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	Of cautery by fire, command to the diseased person to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pierce at their origin, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Many times they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, and ugly and hard scabs; and it happens many times that a black tooth and citrine and worms exist until corruption reaches the gum, and then the tooth becomes stinky. So when you need to have them seen by the diseased person with your hands, and their teeth are in front of yours, remove all until there's nothing left; and do this for the darkness, greenness, yellowing, and other tints, until they're completely gone; if what is removed on the first try is enough, it is good; but if not, you should start again on the second day and third, until you have everything removed. Remember that teeth require different kinds of instruments to be cleaned depending on how their work demonstrates, because the rasp used for removing teeth between them has different forms than those for teeth protruding outwards. These forms and others are prepared with you in mind.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you are treating a tooth for pain that you continue the extraction as long as possible, because it should not be done hastily. This is due to its position so high up in the mouth where one might have an excuse for rushing the procedure.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	When the patient is forced to remove pus, you must be certain of which tooth is causing it. Often the pain indicates the infected tooth, and you should extract a good tooth; but until the infection is completely removed, do not assume all pain has disappeared because we have already done this in these situations; and when you are sure about the tooth causing pain, you must burn around the tooth with hot oil for several spoonfuls to preserve the gum from all sides; then move it to your hands or onto fine tweezers at each pinch until it is well dislocated, then firmly set the tweezers in place; and have the shoulder joint of the infected body part between your knees, and keep it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not jump out on its own, take any of these tools and gently push it in from every part, then move it as you did initially. And if the tooth is pierced and cracked, you should fill it with cloths where the teeth are; and when you extract it softly with tweezers, do not break it during extraction; and you must carefully open around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And make sure you don't break it and leave any part behind. Inform the patient that due to the root's malice, they may experience even greater pain than before. Be cautious not to do this as ignorant healers might, who in their haste and bravado break the tooth once or more times, without considering these precautions; but rather allow the disease to come back every time due to the roots remaining inside or because of the broken tooth parts that remain, just like we often advise. When the tooth is extracted, wash out the socket with wine, vinegar, and salt; and if bleeding occurs (which it often does), wash the socket with vitriol water; and if this doesn't help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, by which you make your teeth first, should be with long points and large handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them have large parts that do not bend upon pulling, and be made of well-forged iron, and have teeth for gripping.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary to place moistened cotton in the mouth with butter for .i. jor or ij days, until the gums are softened. Then pull out the forceps that are called "algefri", making it look like a beak of care; and they should also be made inside just like a file, this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to emerge through all these clamps, it is necessary that you uncover the entire flesh up to the root, and place the instrument called "althali", which is known as palmache, as follows:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be smooth and substantial so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, it's good; if not, use all the instruments you have, as their forms come next:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if assistance is taken with this tool which has two spouts, as shown below:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front according to the order of teeth, and this tool which seems like large pliers, as depicted below:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument not be able to break it, and know that many tools of bone exist; and also other tools, which are not listed; and the wise surgeons find their own tool through themselves, according to what their operations and diseases show them. For there are parts of diseases where the old did not teach any instrument because of the diversity in some and if they break from the carriage or from other bones, or if it decays, then when he searches for the tools that he needs, that I have told you about, and helps with gestures, which is shown here, this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and well holding so as to hold the bone without it escaping, but able to hold and remove it; and then restore in its place the medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, then seek all that instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural form, and the shape is ugly, even in virgin women if it's necessary that you know whether the teeth are grown after the tooth, and they are not in their rightful position, and one cannot pull or file them: then remove them; and if they adhere with the tooth, take this instrument as depicted here, and resembles two small beaks, and should be made of sharp iron at its tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the edge is thin and thin in my hands by the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, so I file with a single file as it is shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like the file used for making needles; and in filing I make the tooth thin and thin in my hands gently, so that you do not move it until it finishes cutting; then smooth out at the end with any smoother, and if its edge is too sharp and hurts the tongue, it's necessary to file down the roughness until it becomes flat, so that it doesn't hurt the tongue or damage speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth rots
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth in front of the socket, or through percussion or falling out, and if the patient cannot press on what he is chewing so that he doesn't defecate, and you have cured it with medicine that restrains, and this proves ineffective; they must be restrained with a thread of gold instead. For threads of silver turn green and rot, but gold never changes. And use threads neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you see the need to straighten the teeth, then take the thread and the needle double between two healthy teeth, then place the dislocated teeth between your own teeth, as long as there are one or more of them. Continue this process until you can see clearly up to a healthy tooth from the other side; then start covering again until you covered that spot before, and pull your hand delicately and carefully, until it doesn't move; and tie your ligature at the root of the tooth so it can’t escape. Then cut out the threads with the pliers, gather them together, and place them between a healthy tooth, and then set it so that it doesn't irritate the tongue; and then leave it like this as tight as it can stay without causing discomfort. And if it loses its position or the threads break, then tighten it with another thread; if it stays and serves well for all its time, and this is the arrangement of teeth and the insertion of two healthy teeth and two dislocated ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth gets dislodged, if you return it to its place, step by step, just as we have said; and don't interfere with anything that isn't suitable or can withstand it, and never make a shape of an ox bone tooth, and put it in the place where the defect is, and tighten it as we have said, and stays and serves this long duration.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the thread of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	No time comes from within the tongue or nature where we are born thus; nor through an accident of sewn wound. The processes are such that you work in your patient's mouth with the disease, have its head over your health, and lift their tongue. Then cut down the nervous ligament as wide as possible until the tongue is dislodged from its place. And if there's hardness or lump, it's due to sudden wound, then pinch the hook and cut the ligament; and ensure that the wound isn't too deep because an artery is nearby. When you are done, lift the head from pinkish water and cool water, then put under the tongue a linen cloth; and cleanse your patient each night so their tongue doesn't stick. And if bleeding occurs, apply vinegar to the head. And if the tongue fails to come back, cauterize with a slow-burning cautery which is good for this case; then cure it with another cure until it's healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that it's of rust color or black or hard, but your patient doesn't feel pain, do not touch it as it is an ulcer; and if it begins to turn yellow and there's moisture, then pinch the hook and drain with a subtle spasm, and release from both sides; and if your tongue fails to come back in your treatment, apply vinegar until it dries out, then return to your work until you have used all force; then lift the head from cool water and salty water, and cure him with other remedies until he is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	from throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	No time comes within the throat cavities which are called 'godath', and they are properly named as two almonds. When you treat them, just like what we said in the division part, and if they remain unhealed, always be careful: if these are pus-filled lumps of small sensation and have a straw-like color, do not touch them with metal tools. And if they are red and their root is large, do not touch them with metal tools as well for blood's escape; but leave them until they're healed completely, then you will remove them, or they would break on their own; and if they have a white color retain, and their root is subtle, prepare your instrument to cope, but first ensure the pus-filled lumps have settled and are in peace. Then make the patient lie under the sun, and their limbs be in good health, expose their mouth, and let the surgeons hold her tongue between their hands, pressing it from all around against the tool; this is how you should do it; use silver or finely made copper as thin as knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue to all this tool, and you see the pus-filled lump, take the tincture and put it into the almond, then pull it up more than you can; and don't remove anything from the layers with it, then push against the tool in a way that resembles pressing something strong; and the head is tied together, one part after another, and they're very sharp, made of silver or copper:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this tool available now, just use tweezers, like this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make cuts on one side and the other; and when you have made a cut in one of the cheeks, then make the same cut on the other according to this same manner, and after the incision gargle with the hot sick patient's saliva, or gargle with both hot and mild water, and when bleeding occurs, then gargle again with hot water, or use cooked green grape pits, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until all of the pus is cleared; then proceed with the treatment until it has healed; and no new abscesses form in the throat other than the two cheeks, so treat them accordingly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, one small abscess. I had almost completely closed the entire throat so much that she could not breathe due to the obstruction and could neither eat nor drink, and died after only about one day or two days. The abscess had risen so high that it had forced out two fluids through the two nostrils. So quickly then, I inserted an inch into one of them, then pulled it out, removing a large portion of mucus; afterwards made another incision near the other nostril, and opened her mouth pressing on her tongue; after this, I inserted the inch in these abscesses, removed part of them, only bleeding out a little bit. And thus cleared the passageway of the throat for the woman, and began now to drink warm water and then wine, not ceasing to cut away at that abscess over long periods of time; and the abscess grew again immediately filling up the space I had emptied until it was very large; then bandaged her up and treated inside the throat with cautery: she remained without growing any more. And left these parts, may only God do good after me.
de l’uve	Regarding the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the head of the shoulder begins to descend within the body cavity and is squeezed and long-lasting, it is called "perpendicular". And if it's bulging and rounded, it is referred to as an "ovoid". When it has been treated in the manner we have discussed earlier during treatment of wounds, but does not improve, and you observe that the removal of pus has subsided, and it exhibits subtlety, then it needs to be handled; and if it's ovoid with a rounded assembly and isn't long-lasting; whether it is blood-red or has an iron color or is black, care must be taken on when making the incision. For there is great risk for the patient here. Therefore, when you see this condition, according to the manner I have described based on its location and size, make the patient face towards the sun, press their tongue with the tool we have previously remembered; then insert the needle into the ovule, drag it outwards, and cut at two-thirds of the three tools we mentioned earlier during cutting through the two amandines. It must be ensured that no unnecessary force is applied when cutting beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more than necessary, it can cause discomfort with speech or words. After making an incision, use what was discussed earlier about cutting through the two amandines and treat until complete healing occurs. And should the patient experience fear during the cutting process, then it is recommended to apply ingenuity during the cautery treatment of the pain area. The manner of the cautery is sharp. And when the disease puts its head into your healthy part, then press their tongue with the tool we mentioned or in the chapter on cautery and apply hot living skin, but not excessively thick nor too thin; and use the movement of that instrument as described above.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let my head have a hair or where we put the medicine, like movements of a spoon, and place the tool with all the medicine on top of the ovule; and make sure the disease stays within its own limit, so that saliva and mucus flow from its mouth into the medicine inside, not descending to the throat or causing inflammation; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it onto the ovule for half an hour's worth of quantity, until you see it absorbed and the reactions to the medicine are calmed down; and if you see this happening, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and place the tool on top of the cotton in the wick above, until the cotton is heated by the ovule; and repeat this often, until the cautery is perfect, then leave it to dry, and cleanse after four or five days. And if you need to start the medicine cautery again, do so, and after the cautery, clean around the ovule with cotton soaked in butter; and rinse from cold water, and gargle until it's healed completely.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or using the cautery; if it's treated with steam according to this method, take calamus, myrrh, and thyme along with rue and chamomile and parsley and similar herbs, and combine all of them or any of these in one pot, put them inside and let it boil; make sure the pot is filled tightly with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot place a hairpin according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And use either silver or iron, and place one of the shoulder blades in the mouth next to the malady until the vapor rises from the gland through the throat; as long as the gland is dead. After that, repeat this often, until the gland dries out, be sure not to do this at the beginning of pus ejection, for many things happen then; and do not perform this technique when the pus ejection is declining. And if this instrument isn't present, take a rod and place an eggshell inside your head so that the mouth next to the malady doesn't become too hot; because the eggshell won't let the vapor weigh down the mouth, it's a good treatment combined with health.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times one finds in the throat bone or spinal part of a fish without anything; therefore, it is necessary that you remove what you can see and press your tongue to the sun with all the instrument until you see movement; and whatever does not open up and remains in the throat, it is appropriate for you to induce vomiting so that the malady leaves as if the meat was cooked in the stomach; by chance if the thing escapes through vomiting; or if the malady swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a small chunk of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when she comes up to your mouth, if she breathes out, and then pull forcefully; and if this does not come out as what we have said, take one tool of thorn according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the forceps be applied to the head so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the head elevated high above; and beware not to touch the epiglottis, lest anything go wrong, nor push any bone inside; and move when the patient pushes the instrument back out, because if it's moved or the thing is slippery; if it pulls down, or if it drags with equal force on all parts of the instrument until it can drag fully.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the lumen of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No single time is medicine administered to the humor of the throat as I have mentioned in the division through treatment with medicines. If this doesn't benefit, then examine the throat of the sick towards the sun. Press their tongue against the instrument that I've told you about. And when you see the humor, draw it out by half an uncia (ancient unit of measurement), or with delicate forceps suitable for this task. Should this not work, take a long piece of hair and place it in the sick's throat near their mouth, then pull out twice as much hair as the length of one iron nail repeatedly. And let them be dipped in cold water all day; take a full cup of cold water and rinse their mouth with it, then swallow slowly while moving your hand frequently; and just as soon as the humor perceives the water, they will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if she does not give birth as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the tool that I mentioned for fumigation of the eye. Do this several times, because it will be without pain. And the method of fumigation is like this: take one pot where there are charcoal briquets and place a cover on top pierced in the middle. In that piercing should go the head of the instrument; then pour your fumigation, put the tip of the herb into her mouth, and close her mouth so that no fumes escape but they move up to her sinuses; and now the mucus will come out, if it does not give birth, repeat this fumigation several times. And make the patient thirsty, feed them salty things and alike, and do not drink water; then she must leave for herself by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to clear mucus is such that when it can be seen, it resembles hooked tweezers for pulling out in the throat; and has a resemblance at the tip as if for trimming, and it has roughness like sandpaper, so what she takes cannot be left behind. And here is the form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	No extraction methods are described according to what memory brings forward from one and another in this book, they vary in perforation and sizing; it is done in two ways out of which one follows its own form and due to the moisture. And the second method is for those located on the body. Because abscesses at the head differ from those at the base, and abscesses on the fatty parts are different from those that come at joints, each has their judgement in operation.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if in abscesses you should not pierce until the body is dead according to its maturation. And if there are such that piercing should be done when they have grown and are not yet dead, as with abscesses at joints. For when abscesses originate at joints, if left until they are rotten inside by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint might become corrupt, which is a cause of contraction in that limb. Or if the abscess is deep within the main member, if you delay the perforation until it is dead, it will harm the main member; or if it's under the foundation, piercing should be done when it is dead; and you should not pierce an abscess which is still growing without completed maturation digestion, except for that one which might have come from deep within the foundation, it wouldn't rot properly inside and would remain buried, causing a fistula; and it couldn't heal properly over a long period.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	It is necessary that you know the time of abscess perforation which occurs according to maturation, and this is when the pain has subsided, and departure of fever, and diminution of pain and heat, and from movement and firmness of the head of the abscess, and other signs; it should be that the perforation stays above or at the level of the abscess, where it opens outwards. And make the perforation long across the body, and if the abscess is near hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and everywhere where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	In those that bend, according to the body part. And when abscesses are in the fatty tissue, you should let the perforation be until it is confirmed by digestion being completed, just as we have said. Because if you puncture before this, it will likely leave the body filled with venom and full of mucus; and might harden the lips and the depths within. And for abscesses that are punctured across the width of the body, according to what the limb needs. It is necessary to make small incisions, small slits; and in large incisions, large slits, and many tears according to the size of the abscess; and if there are such incisions where it's appropriate to clean out the pus, and cover; when it becomes as one piece with a drapery, and has softened, then proceed just like what is done on blisters: and for those that split into three angles, and for those that resemble the leaf of myrtle in terms of how they're covered, such as abscesses of angles; and for those where you make a round incision, and other sizes of incisions and similar cuttings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who lack a head, such as abscesses beneath the skin superficially, it is necessary that you puncture them completely; and when an abscess is large, and it contains a substantial amount of pus, if you drain only part of the pus at once, but take out some portion. Then stop draining until tomorrow, then do not touch anything to the wound; repeat this procedure from large to small multiple times until all the pus has drained; likewise for those with weak strength, or women in pregnancy, or young children, or elderly and decrepit individuals. Because each time there is a jolt of anticipation when the pus discharges, it may cause the patient's condition to worsen, and you might not notice it happening. Therefore, proceed cautiously with this chapter, and when you puncture your abscess, if the wound arises, check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it is a full incision, use linen or old cotton for dressing; and for large abscesses, and there are many slits within, then each slit should be covered with a tent so they lie against each other. And if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin, and tied it tightly, then it is necessary to fill it with old cotton or linens that are moist-proof, and bind until the third day; then heal and apply ointment until it heals properly.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs in your operation, prepare cold water and ease it, and moisten a piece of linen or cloth with two pieces of it, then apply this to the wound repeatedly. And if bleeding persists, ensure governance and cure, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is in ice or cold, and your limb or abscess is heavily muscular, then it's necessary to place moistened tents and cloths on it using wine and heated oil; and if it's internal, and your limb is fatty, then it's necessary to apply moistened cloths with water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day as we have said; then remove and clean the wound and cure it according to what needs to be done, until it heals properly.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know completely in the treatments of abscesses: or I have told you how one should act before treatments of abscesses, and here comes this chapter.
des soros	of the womb
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Or let's consider small abscesses that come from the uterus, and their appearance which resembles a linen cloth like in a rabbit's belly, there are many similarities. There are those with fatness as well as those who have moisture, similar to seeds; and some of them are hard and stony-like for the tailor, and there is no doubt they contain an artery, not acting against it. The action during tailoring involves using all .i. instrument called 'entromissoire', from which its shape follows next: something it contains. If it contains moisture, then make a cut along its entire length. And when the moisture is drained out, then scrape off nothing the skin containing that moisture, as it will return immediately if you leave nothing behind; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, use water and vinegar, and apply this to the wound, leaving it until the next day; and these practices work well when the abscess stays during the night. Then restart the cotton process again as before on the second day, and the third day onwards, until you know for sure that it doesn't stay during the night; then apply ointment cure on this wound with what is suitable, until it heals completely. And if the abscess contains one hard nodule, cut according to this shape along its entire length; and remove all the linings, scrape off from all sides, put your entire treatment for drainage into this cloak where it lies; and if the artery causes you opposition, do as I have told you after. And similarly handle abscesses that are stony, using a tailor's method and then curing in accordance with what I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. And the size above the abscess stone and the moistness, it is lighter because there's less blood. des scrophules	of the scrophula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times an abscess has occurred at the neck, and around the lymph nodes, and in the throat, and not once elsewhere or on the chest, they are small, and they stick to each other. And every scrophula is properly contained within its bone, like a nut and an abscess from the head, as we have said; and there are many appearances of these scrophulas. There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malign and do not obey healing. In this one therefore that you see with good disposition towards treatment, and resembling the color of blood, mute on each side and is neither too close to the neck nor near the artery or in the path, and is not deep; it is fitting for you to touch it from above, and remove from every part, and extend the two lips of the throat up to the lymph nodes, if you need them, as we said with abscesses on the head; and handle gently, and be sure that you do not cut through the nerve or vein, and neither be too deep nor trenching, so that your hand does not escape, and do not look too far ahead, that you do not remove what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this does not allow you to open, put vitriol paste or any powders that stop blood in the wound, and restrain the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed and the wound softened, then begins to rot. And when the blood has stopped, return to your task, as long as you complete it; then judge according to your duty if there are still small nodules remaining, remove them and clean them out. And if the root of the nodule has a large vein, it is not right that you cut this nodule at its root, but tie it with a thick double thread and let it fall through without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then start treating.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you remove the whole nodule, it is necessary for you to assemble the two edges of the wound and sew them now. There should be no excess left because of the size of the nodule; it's necessary that you focus on cutting into the root of it, draw out pus, and sew as we have described. Those nodules caused by excesses, open them up where they break down; then pierce in a similar manner to what was said before, hanging downwardly. After that apply ointment and such things, allowing for corruption; until whatever is infected becomes healthy. And when the wound has been thoroughly cleaned, start treating with ointment applied over flesh until it heals.
de squinance	"De squinance" refers to medical practices concerning deformities or abnormalities related to angles or positioning. It could be associated with conditions affecting bones, joints, muscles, or other bodily structures where the natural alignment is disrupted. This term might cover a variety of scenarios from anatomical malformations due to birth defects, injuries sustained over time, or diseases that alter body parts' normal orientation and function. In medieval contexts, such knowledge would have been part of the extensive medical and surgical practices aimed at diagnosing, treating, and sometimes correcting these abnormalities.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and wrote about neck surgery; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is the inscription of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as "epiglottis" be made; and one should not help this, because all the veins and lungs are near in the body for those who have abscesses deep within their mouth, or in their throat or between two bones.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the bronchial channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary to make the incision through three circles or four, with a small slit going through, between the two circles. The size of the slit does not extend into the cartilage;
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these parts are suitable for cutting the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessel is long inside it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary that they extend the skin of the throat to all the inch, then cut into the bone until it reaches the knuckle; and avoid blood vessels, if you see any sort of thing, and then shape the socket as we have said;
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the cut across the knuckle stream which jumps through the bone that has been broken, and due to loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a bit.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one doubts strangulation, gather the two mouths of the wound as cleanly as possible, and all along the line without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce flesh until it is sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim insists that one should not perform such operations until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient's organs are deemed dead, and the deficiency has been achieved.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	So you cut off the epiglottis because the organs cannot evacuate, and they breathe through the wound, and thus are protected from death;
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And because of this, the ancients instructed to leave the wound open until the disease's malice passes, and it has passed in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and treat it, until it was fully healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw that a maiden took one knife and stuck it in her throat, cutting out part of the windpipe;
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And I was summoned to cure her, and found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found where the blood was issuing from it, and indeed she had no cut veins or conduits other than her throat, and the wind went in through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I acted quickly, treated the wound as much as it was healed;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and there was nothing left for the maiden but to recover her voice and she returned after that to her condition.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Because I say that in the crafting of the epiglottis, do not use fire.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Thick abscesses are called "throat hernia", and they are large, dark-colored swellings, and are very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it occurs in two ways: naturally, and by accident; or natural does not have a cause.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents occur according to two ways, of which one resembles the pus from us, and the other way resembles pus that comes from our arteries;

des nous	From our
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways there are to approach this matter, which I will explain as if it were all similar.
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And so it is fitting for me to describe the whole difference that exists between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that in the state of fever and illness, it lasts as long as the boiling (of bodily processes) has not passed, and is accompanied by putrefaction; thus, once the fever and heat have subsided.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the new there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and contains one yolk, which is its own sack and is according to the color of the body, and begins also like a gooseberry, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	and follows two likenesses, or greasy, or moist, and much of the color are as I said in the division.

When you come to treating the new, you should first inspect and inquire about all the instrument which is called 'entromissory', according to its shape or chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring about abscesses in the new is that you take the wettest part you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers a little bit by little bit, until you know that the instruments have reached the core, then it should be according to the size of the abscess;
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the incisor, and take care not to let it jump.

et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after removing the incisor there is no moisture, know that it was fatty, then cut it in a crosswise manner and take hold of it with forceps. Gently burn each side of it and remove the coat where it lies; do this carefully with a knot to ensure its safe removal.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot remove it intact, remove it piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	For if it stays as it is, it will recur many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it stays for a bit and doesn't bother him, use some corrosive powders on the wound from time to time, keep the wound clean, place soothing substances over pus areas, and treat other wounds until they heal.
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it's a large wound, stitch up the two edges of the wound, and treat the one causing pain due to stitches.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout. Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the instruments for internal treatment, and they come in three ways: large, medium, and small; and among them there are four squares which are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and amongst these there are also three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encompass the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are also like needles used for cutting roots, and they can be made of citrine, or iron, or silver, and yellow needles are preferred over those, and they are more effective than black honey to encompass the bends in fistulas;
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	They come in three types: large, medium, and small, depending on the width of the depressions.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the joints resemble certain likenesses, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if it is joints that have two curves in three different ways;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	and if it is joints with three curves, and they are also in three ways; and if it's joints with two curves, and single-jointed ones, and these are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The top of these is sharp, and there are some among them that only cut from one side, which we call stripping, because in this case one does not cut the vein or nerve;
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And these introducers have their arms restored, so that the patient does not notice them during the incision of abscesses;
