k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	For they do not cut and bleed the wound before the stitch;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then remove the stitches, so that the patient does not become inflamed at night,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and cover the stitches with bandages or cloths to keep them clean and secure.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is healed;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	And this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it requires a needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second type of stitching is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	And it involves sewing together the two layers of leather and two layers of flesh on one needle using a strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	And when you have pierced all four shoulders together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then pull the needle to the place where you started piercing, in the way that one stitches cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch as big as a small coin;
ceste costure sevent li home,	these stitches should bind the fabric,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	And I had a wound where someone had stabbed or punctured, it was deep within the abdomen.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	which had been made by a knife.
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was over a palm in size,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and contained well two palms of intestines,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And there was a wound in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I returned his intestine, and it remained like that for twenty-one hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound was healed up to fifteen days, and I treated it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I would not cure it with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And I would put new clean cloths on the wound twice a day, and wash it with honey water until it was cleansed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper ways of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle and insert it from the outside part until it goes inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the artery straight on, if it has hit the head of the siphon or the costal bone where you have stuck the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and makes it pierce from the other side through the inner part up to that depth.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	And as for understanding this stitch, you do it in the same way as the leathersmiths sew leather,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And as you leave the stitch on one side and then pick it up again from another, until the whole seam is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of sewing, as Galen himself explained,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	It is just like what everyone does, where they naturally join the two parts together,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and they press one of the ends of the thread onto the other end in such a manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	stitch a needle or one of the thread ends close to the skin, and pierce only that side.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	And let both shoulders grow smooth;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	Then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part down to inside.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	for both shoulders are smooth;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce both from the outer part down to inside, using two other smooth shoulders that are on the opposite side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the surgical method of stitches and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien said these words, and none of them testify to it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must stitch the belly with two needles, or if there is thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one should place one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the manner of those who sew joints;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	then the sewing is more painful than in other parts of their belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgement of the wound is like that of the judgement of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just as the art has made it.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you place it back inside the intestine, and the cut; then apply a stimulating powder on top.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the wound is swollen, apply no ointment until the injury subsides;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew the thread, and stitch up the cut, and bind it.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound as usual until it heals.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	And if you don't have medicine, just place it above, as soon as it starts to drip honey, old cotton,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and stir it twice a day until it is thoroughly cleaned.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you do not need other medicines in various preparations if the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound might affect the principal limbs,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	If it is necessary for you to moisten with a light oil of tempered heat, or in rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it inside the joints, and over the elbows;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or gangrene in the bowels, and this happens many times,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if you use black wine enemas, and similarly if the gangrene reaches up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce within it, and know that when it's large intestine, it is lighter to heal than the small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called 'young' cannot be healed if it is injured,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	And that's because of the placement of the veins and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to the nerves in relation to its nature.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the scab jumps over the wound, you should put it back just like an intestine while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it is old and turned towards red or black, then you should bind the one that is black, so that no blood spreads there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the band;
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place both shoulder blades above the wound up to beyond it on each side to ease the extraction when the ribs are removed, and for the wound to heal.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestines are involved, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	If it can be restored in any way,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen that a person was pierced by a lance or through the belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	And the wound was located on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And it became inflamed and formed a fistula, causing malnutrition and discomfort;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied the treatment according to what I could do, and didn't stop refining until it was healed, and bound up the wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw that they had stuck together, I feared that there might be discomfort in their stomach;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	And there was no harm, but remained in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And it is said by some experimenters that when there is a small injury inside the intestine, it must be treated in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take large seeds of garlic, then join the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the garlic has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	If it constrains her mouth upwards;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then he holds her head, and this is done so that she cannot release herself;
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then places another restraint in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely treated;
et cout la plaie.	and heals the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	Those who get too hot in their intestines, and do not cause any harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine,
en teil maniere:	in such a manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestine thread so that most of it is dried,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	And then to the head of this thread .1. a fine linen thread twisted,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then knot the thread at the needle, sew it through the intestine, and set the dislocation in its passage;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing the ruptured intestines is not to be done without considering the path of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it's in one of the intestinal loops, if there is no injury or sickness, you must use subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of a fistula, or if it be one
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and similarly when it is pierced and bled.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the truth of a hard and whitish concretion, where one does not feel pain,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	it is also as hairy as a bird's feather;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it is clear and thin, and at other times thick;
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes it is insufficient, and at other times enough.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken about the classification of wounds, that every wound that is not healed and contains no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	This comes from none of the seven causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	It is to say, by the diminution of blood or pus;
ou por sa malice;	or through its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard flesh within and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to grow;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	where there's too much blood;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or when the limbs are swollen, and the material is of poor quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or when the medicine isn't good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because it's like a plague due to corruption;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	For because of its position in the area is late the digestion, and delayed the healing, and flees naturally;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	For there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the treatments with medicine in this section.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or it is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of fistulas which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	You know that fistulas occur in all body parts;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that originate from the large veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the stomach, or in the intestines, or in the bladder, or in any of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or in the spinal column of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	And if at times one comes to possess the property of the main limb, and knows its nature.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are difficult to heal, and there is nothing else but labor, and lack of knowledge;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not reach up to what I have said, and you have taken the treatment for it,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and you should recognize them. If you take a spider's web or iron rod, if the fistula is straight, you will see it;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	And if the fistula is twisted, then seek with a subtle probe to straighten it,
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the twists will bend and move along with the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has turns that are hard to follow even with attempts to probe it,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	if you try to use a catheter through one of those turns,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for moisture moves from one part to another, and cleanses;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then carefully inquire with your power, so you know if there's bone or nerve, and feel it completely,
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient about the pain they feel when your hand presses on them, and specify where they feel it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you truly know the location of the pain, and whether it's far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	In none of the limbs that I have mentioned, if the cut is made as I have instructed,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and for the scabbard and the rotten shafts that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then the treatment until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the sinus tract goes down to its proper depth straight, you should follow it up as far as possible, no matter how deep.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	Then I place moistened wicks in the astringent medicine, and fill them up to the opening of the ulcer.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	Until the medicine eats away the excess that has remained at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And then I place bandages made of healthy flesh until it is sound;
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it doesn't become sound through this means, then cauterize it as we have described,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And if the bone has rotted from the ulcer, then it is treated.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerves are damaged or affect main limbs, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	And if the bone is exposed, and there's decay and darkness, then remove it until all decay has been excised.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then clean the area around the affected bone as long as it remains healthy;
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	And if there's no strength, and returns back just as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	you know that you have not gone all the way to the end:
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	search and seek until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all decay, then return it to its proper place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	And if he is so healthy, this is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	But if not, know that corruption has spread too far, and you cannot bring it back;
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	if there is no other option but to leave it to natural processes;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there's just a small infected bone, and you can extract it using forceps,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	if you extract with an instrument suitable for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, treat them all, do not leave any out;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture causes it to go against you, and there is no doubt or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	and if it cuts and moistens and burns, and frees the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place something stench-inducing on the wound.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and let it be until the bones are rotted inside the flesh.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will have the bones with less resistance;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	if you are to rule for as long as the decay lasts, until all of the blackness is entirely removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large portion of corruption, and it reaches up to the flesh around the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	if it suits, you should sear and cover until it reaches the point of corruption, and then treat until it is healed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	And I will tell you of a case involving a fistula that occurred in one's leg.
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take an example and help yourself in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	There was once a young person around thirty years old, who experienced pain in their leg due to an issue that came from within the body.
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	The matter traveled to the leg and there formed a large abscess; no external reason could be found for opening it.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	yet the surgeons due to their enthusiasm opened them so far that they reached the abscesses,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they corroded very little material, and created a fistula, and much of the damage caused all to weep blood and bodily fluids from their wounds;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many patients took treatment for about two years, and there was no wise person in the art of surgery,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I have been called upon, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	And what grows through the narrow passages with great force;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	And became red on the cheeks like youth's flush, and had a yellowish hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I made a tent in one of these narrow passages, and then searched all the passages,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and found that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I quickly did so, and cut on one of the rough edges until I revealed a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and found it decayed and pierced through, with the decay extending up to the inner bone;
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I was the one who appeared before me from the decayed bone, and I thought that there was no other decay, only what I had taken away;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and began to restore the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not heal it;
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then began again, and revealed the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	I found that the decay continued within the bone, and the soreness, and then I removed it, and bent to join up the head.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I did not go as far as to match within a palm of the bone, and I took it all the way back to its original location.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I set it with medicine; and he was healed and joined quickly.
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	And it can no longer start over with the procedure except due to the weakness of the illness, which cannot bear it.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	And because of the fear of death that I have for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For the blood loss often occurs, but it was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and there formed within the bone a tough flesh, and it was well arranged and had no harm or opposite effect at all in every way, neither inward nor outward.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if any bone is broken within the body, it should be treated in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	Take hold, and pull at the tip of the bone that sticks out,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command him to extend it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	And place another thread of wool that is thicker than the first thread, and bind it over the skin which lies inside the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	And stretch the head, so that you draw out corrupted flesh from within.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	Then expose the flesh on the bone where you see sinew, making sure the sinew doesn't tear the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place one piece of charcoal or a board under the bone to cover the rotten flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And it must happen just as one can see and feel the decay, and decay again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is rotted, and doesn't open, and the decay is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	if you find the flesh has decomposed completely; then place a single coal over it;
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then apply the decay from one part to another, and let the heat of the cloth last as long as the decay lasts, just as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And if corruption is within the joint, then treat the corrupted joint, and be it bone or contains something on the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And if corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then treat it if there's no other way to correct it;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	And if corruption is at the base of the hand or foot, or very strong in that matter,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	Nevertheless, it must be asked how this corrosion opens to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	And make it clean in all ways that you can, but that the vein or the nerve do not hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	Know that the knife and the saw are many for cutting these bones, depending on their position and the appearance of the bones,
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their size and their fineness, and their strength and their weakness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And it is necessary to equip oneself with each type of work according to the tool for its operation;
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	And know that the book will show you the tool you need, according to the knowledge of this craft.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the evidence of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	if you consider the tool you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The shoulder gets dislocated either due to an internal cause, or due to an external one;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	And when you have treated that corrosion with the cure of medicines, and they do not benefit from it,
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	So one must cover that limb up to the joint where the corrosion comes.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	If the patient dies through this cause of death, or through the evil, which is greater, due to the fault of the limb;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	And the signs show when the limb turns black, as if it has been scorched by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	And after the darkness, then comes that member-corrosion part by part,
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and spreads throughout the body; if you hurry with copper treatment,
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and it is by the impact of certain venomous beasts, such as sea spiders and vipers and similar creatures,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	If the corrosion is at the head of the second finger, if you cut it, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, if you cut at the joint, so that the corrosion does not extend up to the arm;
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	And if it goes up to the arm, if you cut where the hand meets the arm; and if it passes the elbow mark, this is where death comes.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	It's not worth any remedy beyond its quantity of virtue;
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	And do this until the corrosion or rust comes or occurs: if it comes at the first joint, you clean up after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes or sticks, you cleanse all of the stick;
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends into the leg, you cleanse at the knee joint;
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other way except for causing death to the patient.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	And the method for covering or bandaging a limb is such that you bind it above and below,
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and spread a strip of cloth under one of the straps and another strip above the other strap.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	then you should cut away the flesh that lies between the two straps to form a one-inch wide opening, until the bone is exposed;
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cover it with bandages or cloth, making sure that neither of them touches the healthy skin,
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And to the patient brings about another injury and pus-laden wound.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And when bleeding occurs during your work, if you quickly cauterize the area,
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put some constraining powders on it; then return to your medicine until its completion,
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the limb with a reliable bandage, and treat it until it is healed;
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened at one household concerning it:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a blackness that seemed like the mark of fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and this burn came first on his thigh, spreading until it consumed all the thigh;
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the wound became visible, he would cover his thigh, and he became healthy;
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	And long after, there was the healing of the cut or burn from the hand, and it came to me,
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I placed things that rebounded after the purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosion;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wished for me to touch his hand, but I would not, that I might have hope of rebounding the substance;
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I doubted also that if I cut off his hand, he would die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	Because the powers of the earth were weak; and he despaired altogether, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and held up his hand in defense, and was cured.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And I have only recounted this story for anyone who needs to do it differently, if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	No abscess ever comes in the inner part of meat, and stays so long that it causes a large assembly of worms;
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And then they will drill and puncture, and the arrow jumps, and the arm remains within you, like some vessels;
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	And the skin above is also as thin as a single layer of fabric.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	And they do not go all the way to the bone or nerve, and such diseases are called "safe".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And it is not called "fistula";
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	However, if it's so long that it comes up to the bone completely, then it is called a "fistula";
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and in cooking if you cover that skin entirely, and similarly when it's delicate as with a piece of fabric;
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and doesn't rot due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have heated the skin so that it cooks through, and corruption hasn't reached fully,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And the skin is thick with flesh, if the treatment for catarrh is like this:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	Look if his breasts are large, and the belly under them has a rank smell,
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Then use an Egyptian cathartic medicine as described below:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	Take saffron, oil, and litharge, equally, and cook them in a pot on the fire for one hour,
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	While the medicine remains red, and thickens similarly to honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and prepare it in water and honey,
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and give an enema to the abdomen, and restrain the convulsions;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	let the medicine stand for two hours, then strain it out;

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	From the abscess of the nail

Des vils	Of the mean or lowly born.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Their veins are thick-walled and filled with various excesses of melancholy, extending to multiple members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And more happens to legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry than to others.

Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron treatment follows two methods: one involves bleeding, where black blood is extracted;

De la voinne civile	From the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is found in the legs, on warm parts where no herbs or trees grow, and in soil without moisture;

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cattle disease", because it often affects cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and travels throughout the body up and down,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And one feels it well across each limb by limb, until they reach the skin where it was, and jumps forth;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is infested with putrefaction from some body fluids, if they approach and twist like snakes and worms or roundworms in the abdomen;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is doubt about its nature, for when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	By chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and bled, one can only say when it begins:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then it is necessary that you bind the shoulder above and below with a strong bandage tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut and bleed it, and if its wound is properly inside the flesh, you will not find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you apply a fire cautery there, until it heals;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greatest harms it causes are when they go to the eye, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming close to the eye or head, then restrain it with your fingers near its root, then cut upwards, and pull forcefully;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	It is necessary to use the herb for cleansing body fluids from medicinal solutions for those ailments caused by bodily humours,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And if it involves meat that causes putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain coming from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it's a pain that comes to any parts of the body,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And it spreads from limb to limb; and I saw what I told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was summoned to tend an ill woman, and she showed me her arm, revealing a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And one hour after, the wound would rise as if an animal had bitten at his shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	more quickly than anything else, like freshly cut silver when it's taken from its place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that side, and entered the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then it began to turn within my body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled greatly at how she moved member by member within my body, for I had never witnessed this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I have seen many instances where the pain of the affected area moves to another place,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I did not experience it myself, as I see it in the woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought it was because of this that the woman had smooth skin, and her veins exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And from this, one can see the constriction caused by the wind;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Yet, those who are in good health and have moist skin and covered veins do not show this according to this reason.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the treatment of this illness, and if the patient feels pain as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the treatment begins quickly above and below it, then apply heat until that wind-strength is constrained within them;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and treat the area with a cautery; and if you don't see it at your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if there is treatment for someone suffering from wind disturbances, such as stinking pills, pills made of the rattlesnake, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are various depending on their shapes and according to where they pierce or hit the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety of these things is that some have large points, and others are small, and some are barbed, and some are soldered;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and there are those that have two edges, and those with tongues, and those where pieces are attached;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and she who pierces any member does so in two ways: or piercing the main body,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	Like brain, heart, liver, spleen, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar body parts.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it concerns that part of these members, and the signs of death, which I will tell you later, you'll see:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	So it is necessary that you prepare for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when that bad sign does not appear and the arrow is not fully removed, you should pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the symptom of a brain injury when an arrow pierces the bone, and jumps over the structure that is above the brain,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is characterized by blindness and numbness and inversion in vision, and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and reddening of the tongue, and seizures and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And perhaps there is loss of smell or hearing; and sometimes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	It might have a white moist wound appearing like pimples, and in that case it also resembles burnt flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And if you notice this sign, keep with your treatment, and pull out the arrow if it's still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it bleeds or stings indicates that it is close to the left breast, and also feels as if it is stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow also stops moving like the hair, and in black blood comes out, and brings coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	So you can have no doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that one should not ignore is when foam does not come out from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns red, and they sigh loudly with a quivering cold.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow is found in the covering over the buttocks, it is located below the small ribs; and produces great pain and sighing; and all the limbs move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow is in the stomach by chance, then there would be nothing of undigested meat coming out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow is found in the belly or abdomen, and there's no passage of bile through the intestines, then there's no hope for treatment or extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow is stuck in the bladder, causing urine to spurt and escape, and patients feel intense pain: know that this wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, including the arms and shoulders, neck, throat, collarbone, shoulder blades, spine of the back, ribs, chest, and legs, as well as seeming members, are safe according to several different positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When an arrow is in the body's nerve or artery and it is not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do that treatment.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one person where an arrow struck or entered the back of the neck at the base of the nose:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it, and from the other side removed along with the ear's fat, causing no significant discomfort.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And tried to extract an arrow that had penetrated the oil's fat from under the paper.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	The arrow was embedded, and I could only reach its tip towards the shaft.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	The arrow was of great length compared to an Ottoman bow, about 1 inch thick without feathers; the extraction went well, and no harm befell it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And remove an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and was the Arabic arrow in his ear:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I cut the barbells, and sharpened until I pulled it out, and freed the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And remove an arrow from one's body, where it was stuck in the back or belly, and I feared that he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after having passed thirty days, if his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, and removed it, and forced it out, and there was no bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you have an arrow that has fallen or stuck in a person's back, and the wound is healed at the site;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and keeps the arrow inside, and does not alter its natural position,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And to another man, who was hit by an arrow in his face, and the wound was closed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained like this enduring great pain; and many others similarly.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And he shot an arrow at one of the king's two sons, who had it stuck in his neck,
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly leaning to the right side; and the arrow was fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called for treatment after she had been bleeding for three days. I found the wound to be very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried it with all my subtlety and did not feel it at all;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	And there was no feeling or pain throughout her right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I place on his head absorbent and digesting plaster, because his head does not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I saw the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put on the plaster for several days and quickly healed the wound, then let the patient rest long.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he felt the arrow within his nose for one day; and he told me this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I apply a corrosive medicament to the wound for as long as it is open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow that was moving towards his shoulder;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I adjusted it by applying that corrosive medicine to the wound through the opening, until the head of the arrow became clearly visible;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	And pierce well the ends within four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	Then spread the wound if it allows to grip with the pincers, and move my force on both sides, and cannot escape;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	So I continued refining and devising ways to use tools, until I had it for one day with well-made pincers,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to how its shape will come at the end of this chapter, as long as I treat it, and heal the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And they judge that the cartilage at the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I will restore it then, and once it is sewn up, it will be healed completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	I told you about the quality of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your attention on what I do not say, because books cannot understand everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but the wise doctors compare on quite small matters, and on what is current and lacking,
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	in true number work, and nine instruments, for the removal of foreign matters which occur in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows are stuck in limbs according to two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	By the elbow where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And that which jumps in through the wound or enters it is an arrow entering into its flesh, and for no other time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump in now, let it grow until the body is hardened inside, and let it be released from that point.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And likewise if it is embedded in the bone and cannot be released, let her stay like that for some days, and remove her every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, should penetrate through all one slender hole, as long as the inside of the leg is widened, and then guide it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the lungs of the brain,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the incidents that I have described are open to the patient: if he does not remove it, but leaves it until its edges become even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the arrow comes up to the sinew, this is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrow is only fixed within the bone and does not penetrate to its depth,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And remains the patient free from any harm for several days without a bad incident, if the process goes well.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is so deeply embedded and cannot come out, then apply hot fomentations internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow has been returned inside the body so that one cannot see it, then seek it thoroughly with all effort;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, guide it with any suitable tool;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot by the tightness of the wound, and by the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is neither bone nor nerve or vein, cut it as long as the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and remove the arrow if you can, and if there are ears attached to where the arrow is held,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if there's bone that is stuck inside of you for two parts at the joint where you can feel,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrow's ears until you can draw it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And do it skillfully so as not to break the arrow, making its extraction more painful.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it in one go, leave it until the shaft is completely rotten up to the elbow, then try again, for its extraction is easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if bleeding against you runs contrary, then apply what we have instructed about treatment according to our chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	And beware of incisions near nerves and veins, and apply as you can carefully extract the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	Either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and treat the patient according to how they were before the arrow fell.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	This is the greatest help for you, and if you cannot do it, then follow what the sign tells you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it opens any part of him, or if the skin is swollen in some place where you see it or feel it differently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Therefore cut there, as long as the tongs can take hold, and then press: if jump now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, twist your hand around as long as she enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull her.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave her still, and then start extracting again until she comes out;
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if he has an arrow wound, then he holds the entire shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it's in the stomach, and you see to apply surgery, so I administer one instrument made of hair;
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow penetrates into the hair of the tool; and then apply force,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if the arrow is covered in hair, I use one instrument with a pointed end to assist in extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow is touching, then it must be that you grasp all the meat inwardly where I enter or exit, if you can,
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits or pierces the head or stomach or bladder or side, and it is close to vital organs, then you can cover it up if you can;
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cover the artery and the nerve, then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if that is your skill.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment as long as it's healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tongs used for arrows resembles an eye, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And in various ways: large, medium-sized, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the fletching is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To push at the tip of the arrow, as it is shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the forceps to push and retrieve is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of veins from common causes
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins through which we drain blood are thirty-one, of which there is an average of sixteen.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means: Two small ones that are behind the ears, they are called the 'two herbechs';
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries that are in the two visible temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, they are called 'aspires';
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is on the forehead; and the vein that is at the nose part of the head;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are on the lips above the mouth, and these are the veins which are called "aeugherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are underneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins which are commonly treated are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it runs along the left ribs, and they call it the laymen's "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the middle one is called 'fast', and it consists of the cephalic vein and the basilic vein,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it 'the vein of the heart' by laymen; and the basilic either runs along the right or left side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call this medical procedure "the opening of the belly's vein", and it is performed on the back.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one about which they heal, which becomes evident when it opens upon the sack.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salvation is the vein that's located between the index finger and the ring finger, and if it's two inches in length;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And on the leg and at the ankle there are three veins: one is below the bend of the calf near the left side of the body,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second sentence that is at the ankle bone on the right side; and the vein which is called "nurse", that is located in the ankle of the other side;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And on the other leg are three veins beneath them.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are behind the ears so aids in earache and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of a healthy person, as I tell you, are such that you need to allow the hair to grow long and evenly; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub or scrub the area where the veins are with a coarse cloth; then pinch the lump of the diseased area tightly with a pin.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	Until the two veins appear behind the ears at the level of the shoulder:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	Place your hand here, and when you feel the pulse near your neck, listen carefully to this advice;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the scalpel and guide the needle through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all the way above the vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut and skin and the vein properly, so that two inches thick will be pierced, and let out blood as long as you see it;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then tighten and hold until it heals.
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already spoken of the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The healing of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it goes to old embrocation,

puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lifts the knee above the vein at your second finger tip, and holds the scalpel against it.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	then lift the vein upwards, and clamp it, just like you did with other two veins, and let the blood flow according to your need;

et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then make the dislocation again, and keep it until it heals; and we have spoken about this as well as its treatment and removal, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The treatment for the vein in the forehead is equally effective as that for the frontal artery when dealing with diseases of the face like migraine and fever.

Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and press with your hand or another thing, and let blood flow according to the amount you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the neck of the patient, and tie the vein as long as it is healthy and there are no times when blood comes out from a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Always, it must not be that the flames are too much; and heal across because the bone is close, and by chance break the flames when they are delicate.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in these two eyes aids with the eyes, at the nose, and at the jaw, and in the ear canal in the ear, and for diseases of the cheek;

puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then heal it, and let the healing pass through, a bit long like a flame a bit wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, by chance they break; then do a correction with blood, as much as you need, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The surgery for bleeding near the nose involves the use of an instrument, and it is performed separately from uncanniness, and in diseases of the face,

car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the vein does not open properly when it is being done, and the wound will now start to heal.

et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is like the shape of a flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two kidneys helps with constriction of the artery and beginning of mixing processes, and is associated with many diseases, and pus formation, corrosion, and herpes infections, and tumors;
