et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And alleviate the pain when there's concretion or stone, if it alleviates by its attractive force by chance, or empties the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus does she when placed upon the liver and lungs if there's retained suction,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these suction cups are administered empty to suck only; and they are not administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	As for the remedies of such weeping diseases, and in this manner one should fill the wet sponge with hot water, or with water that has cooked the useful herbs necessary for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction tool used at fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two and a half inches in length from the bottom, and at its midpoint on each side there is one small protrusion, just like to pierce a needle,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be made of iron or wood so that it does not blister the patient upon placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And there is in the middle a pole across like an arachnid or iron, for placing a candle in hand.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	And let them be large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suck-pipes for children are different from those for adults, and those that are thin compared to those that are fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one must place this suck-pipe on the limb like this:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a candle wax plug or one line segment, and place it inside the suction cup on top of the penis that is inside the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the heat is at the bottom of the suction cup and does not burn the foreskin;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and you should do so at the part that we have said, so that when you want to, if it goes off as vapor, and removes the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the line segment as before, and repeat this often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the suction cup method which is used in pleurisy illness, during all stages of fever, there should be neither a lack nor an excess; it should only be administered when it's full with water and placed on the body only.
et c’est li forme:	and it is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Tongue sucking should only be performed when limbs cannot have suction cups due to their small size such as lips and gums, or similar cases;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	And on the underside of the horse's muzzle, such as hooves or noses, or other similar cases;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And concerning the quality of the user, if you find veins that are in sweet waters without clotting when clean, then you take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	And place a nut in sweet water until they become familiar and have nothing in the stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	Then proceed to bleed and use suction cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place them on the veins;
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and gape open, if you can place suction cups there, then do so, for this works quite well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the limb with warmth and water well, then rub it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the skin becomes too hot after the course of the arrows, moisten it with one.1 cloth dipped in cold water and place it there until the arrows are extinguished;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if there are multiple arrows, apply ground vitriol or garlic and similar substances until they are extinguished;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Or you place half of peeled beans on the wound, and let them dry on the wound, which will stop bleeding now;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more knowledge, take other ways.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the veins don't want to be taken, rub the site with fresh blood, or you insert a needle there until blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them, and as soon as they sense the blood, they will start to move;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle a little aloes and ground meal on them, or ash; now they will start to heal.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine and the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear son, that the leaves of these chapters contain things unseen in any old books; no one has ever seen them or read about them from letters.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And because of this reason, the knowledge has been estranged in our land, for I have never found anyone who knew well;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of this, ascribed to the knowledge of ancient books or from studying them so much that I dealt with this art, through experience, and through familiarity with my life's routine;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in these two chapters previously.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it follows that we should outline the preface of this book, which covers the essence of speech and chapters where one's intelligence is engaged. We must remain truthful, so those who have experienced this know and learn this noble art, and also teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that if any fracture, dislocation, twist or sprain occurs in any body part, it is necessary to immediately treat the patient from both sides simultaneously and separately, without causing him discomfort, whether due to frailty of the body, young age, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the cautery is too tight or too cold; and eating cold jousts, meaning cold meats, and liver and venison, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill your body with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have doubt about an abscess becoming hot, or spreading of matter in the limb; so improve the patient's health to their former state as they used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones start to heal, it is necessary that one cooks the meat that causes excessive cooking or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and chestnuts, and peas, and cow's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this kind of cooking leads to more movement and heals the breakage faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that bones broken in old or feeble people do not return to their natural state of being well attached or fused, due to the dryness of the limbs, nor are those also too tender, such as children's bones.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but do not abandon its cure, reset the broken bone. On large pegs that fit and join the limb together, as long as it is pushed just like before; and do not hurry in its work, for this requires fattening with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures come in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	But the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you all about fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is damage heading towards harvest, and another when sharpening, such as the cut of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if in damage with injury, and breakage with a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each way has its tool, and its proper instrument for restoration, according to what memory brings to its place;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known by the breakage of the bone through where the limb twists and opens well outward, and is compressed under the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or misalignment of the joint, and the body does not feel great pain, if there is no break;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have twisting, or a crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the following remedies, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that when the break occurs internally and the two parts are disjointed, you should now put them at an equal point, so that the abscess is in line with the wound.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if pus is present, if he leaves it for no day, until the pus is relieved;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then place it evenly as you can lightly and carefully, knowing that the restoration of this is easier than when there are pieces involved. Then extract it, according to this later instruction.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it's divided into two parts, whether it involves hands or feet, or at your hand if it's a small limb, or divided by two strings, or one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And place the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the injured member are removed, you reset it by all means into its original position as you can, and be sure to avoid causing any further injury or pain through your work.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And correctly align the ends of the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with your hand if you think it is not quite right: if the dressing is beautiful and do not strain too much; do not squeeze as those who bring about pus discharge and muscle contraction in their work, as we have desired many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is to your satisfaction, restrain well the patient so that they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, while turning or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and see to it that the limb is secured so that the patient does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, if it's not at all to his liking, then you should put him in a state of rest so that he doesn't feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and see to it that he is placed properly straightened, making sure there's no twisting when he is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	the quality of the broken limb should be according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs vary in size, degree, and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs such as arms and legs, and similar things; so it is necessary to wrap them with soft and fine linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And those that are larger, such as the buttocks and calves: it is necessary to wrap them with a broad and firm bandage, for the wide bands embrace the entire large limb and restrict it equally from all sides, so there is no unevenness;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then wrap with lighter bandages around three times or four according to the member, and press your hand slightly along the entire bandage, then go above the breakage and restrain less, so that the breakage moves away a little from the breakage;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the bandage gradually and gradually, until you have covered a large part of the healthy area, then apply another bandage, and wrap it around again near the broken area;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the site of the fracture, and apply pressure moderately, not too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the previous chapter.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the tied threads of linen or cloths as long as they are equal in length, then bind it all over with a bandage, and then put your well-made stars on top; if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place on something that soothes the abscess and removes the swelling, and leaves it like that for a few days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then apply pressure over the stars, and they should be of half the width of a thick cane, or from the wood used for making fishing nets, or from palm leaves, and they should follow this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But it is necessary that the iron which one places above the burn be a little larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it fits the size of the limb whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then fix it on the irons in the same way you did at the first application, then tie an additional piece of thread above it, just as you tied it above the burn at the first application;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	make sure there is less tightness than before; and it should be that the thread be of medium size, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as in works of wool that make their loops out of twisted linen cords, and this is great error, because the loop cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not suit for there to be less than half a dou (a unit of length) between each element.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are irritated by the pins after pressing them in their healthy places, put patches of linen or wool on them, so they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is swollen and the joints are broken, I will tell you the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know that it is not fitting to restrain all broken limbs for the whole first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not fitting to put stays on them for their entire first five days or ten, or more depending on your confidence in each particular case occurring.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the way of the ancient plaster methods for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that stays on the mill walls and mix it with plenty of egg. Make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick, and use it; this is the common method of using plaster to restore fractures in various ways, as well as for women and small children because it isn't too harsh or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations: take 3 barley grains and garlic and mint and asafetida and gum arabic and myrrh, each in .x. 3 grams; and incense and aloes, each in .v. 3 grams; vinegar is also needed, .viiij. 8 grams; grind these into powder, then mix with plenty of egg; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster, for it has a good composition, restoring broken bones quickly, and is suitable for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way to plaster for twisting: take mugwort and myrrh, each of .xiii.3; frankincense and aloes, each of .viii.3; achillea vi.3; boric acid .x.3, grind well together, mix with vinegar or enough egg yolk, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another way to apply a plaster for broken bones and exposed joints, and to soothe the arising pain, and the use of bone cutting and bruising: take new wool, and its fat in broth and oil cooked, and put it on the wound. This plaster does not heal completely, but it is better for soothing abscesses and properly relieving pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method for dressing when restoring bone fracture and easing the removal of pus. Take root of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, ground ivy, one part from each; grind it all together with wine, then apply this mixture to any heated limbs. If not hot, mix with damp coriander water or plain water, and use it accordingly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another more vigorous method than the first when pus is being restored from the limb. Take roots of valerian, and flaxseed, borage, alfalfa, and sorrel, as well as violet and chamomile flowers, one part each; grind it all together with salt water, or sweetened water, or wine, depending on the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates instructs that to restore strength in the fractured limb, one should apply a balm made from beeswax and oil, and nothing else, more. He states it should be of neither too soft nor too hard texture.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that we should place on the broken limb to restore it, things dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of plastering that is useful for injury and pain: take mutton and feathers from cooked sheep or bird feathers, and mustard, and equal salt, and grind them together, and make a plaster with it and use it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then after a while, take care not to let the patient feel any pain, nor does their bone move in its place; if it is done without hands working.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching comes to the limb, or there is no rest or swelling, then hurry up and remove it, and apply the plaster now; take a lightweight cloth and a wet sea sponge, dip it in water, and immerse the limb until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, moistened in water or oil rose, and bind it with a bandage until you are sure of removing the cautery completely;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation settle on the limb, and relieve the pain, then continue with the treatment subtly, and a little plaster, and don't strain it as strongly as before; and treat it delicately until it's healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus and redness, pain, and swelling are present everywhere on the wound, and you need plastering and bandaging, then start again, just as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said comes to the limb and if it was not released until after three days or four, or five, or seven; and each time leave it for twenty days, according to this, as long as the healing progresses and brings closer the adjustment of flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore hold the restraint more than at first, and make him fatten his flesh, as I said earlier; and if you see that the left side dries too much than necessary is, know that no remedies can come.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then use hot water baths every time you reset it, and do this once every three days, and drain a bit of the joint fluid;
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this procedure then cut off the remedies from the limb, and hasten what the foolish people do, that bend the member wrongly: it is bad, and there are many dangerous outcomes, and I see no other thing than to rest and have it done straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Regarding the various methods of crushing.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of breaks exist, and various shapes occur, and their causes are categorized;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For there are breaks caused by the impact of a sword, and in the neck bone, it breaks up to the symphysis which is below the vertebrae, like when a mallet hits or a staff is thrust; this method of breaking is called "hatchet break".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword penetrates through the bone from above to below, it is called this method of breaking "absolute"; and these are the large or small injuries from these two types of breaks.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack in the stone, or through stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a break close to the membrane beneath the bone or on the bone itself, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there is a wound that penetrates the bone as finely as a hair, and this crack is small, thus such breaks are called "hairline" fractures;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with stone or falling or from any other cause, and a piece of bone enters the cavity beneath it, causing the bones to rub against each other like when blacksmiths hammer on their anvils; and the stone enters the inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more in those who have wet bones below, such as in an adult's skull;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And applies to all these methods of breaking down where small fragments are removed, such as seeds; and I will discuss this in its proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breaking through by removing them from above, and the inquiry into tests, and through corruption in the flesh that is upon it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed it in, if the black break appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the breakage, be careful of adverse events due to the disease, and if you see no bad adverse event, such as vomiting bile, loss of appetite, expansion, fever, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, do not hesitate in diagnosis.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming mishap, yet you hope for salvation, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when winter comes first to you and it is in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fifteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the pus around the bone becomes putrid, and the accidents that we have said occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone break reaches just beneath the membrane covering the brain, you should split the broken part like this: and then take the head from the patient, expose it on the bone in all the ways that you can, and under the shape of the wound as much as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And if blood flow is necessary to uncover the bone, or when an abscess cavity opens up, you should use whatever aids are appropriate, and here it's recommended that you fill the area with wet cloths infused in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And let the wound rest until the abscess pain subsides and blood flow is assured; then begin by incising through to the bone. This can be done in two ways as prescribed: One method involves cutting directly in front with a narrow incision, which results in this shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And make another cut slightly larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you should have several different-sized cuts: some narrow and others wide, with each being sharp-pointed and made of iron; and when working on them lightly, ensure that you do not injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is too hard and doesn't penetrate, you must puncture it internally in such a way that you administer cuts with needles, not too deeply so they do not pierce beyond the bone's thickness, and there should be a margin of about one circle above the point, ensuring that the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than one, so that each goes to its place within the width of the bone, for you need needles for all sides; this is how three kinds of needle formations are:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing internally through the broken bone is to place one needle on the bone, and turn with your thumbs until you know that the bone has pierced. Then replace the needle a little further elsewhere, and do this all around, then cut in between the perforations of the bone which is located between the teeth, and do it more subtly than possible and gently as we have said, continuously until you pull out the bone to your hand or with no tool that you have such as forceps; and make sure not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is appropriate that you scrape away the bone remnant attached to the bone with an instrument similar to a tooth, but it must be more robust and finer than another tooth.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if it stays in place with no small bones or scales, if you gently manipulate them with two instruments; then treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of doing it is what Galien stated, which is more prudent; and he uses a lot of force, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you should expose a part of the bone, at or near where the break appears to move, so that once you have exposed this part, you will place underneath the tip of this lens-shaped incision, with which we are dealing here:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and make the incision halfway between two ribs, so that you are cutting towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer from above, gently breaking the entire bone, and be careful not to damage the membrane beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it's pressing against the bone, gently pull the bone, because there is good sensation of discomfort and fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone breaks without piercing through the membrane, and the bone is cut only above, and there are small fragments, then you should proceed after that roughness, and remove the scales using a fine razor. You must have different quantities of this tool to apply in each area most appropriately, according to the work and the appearance of the breakage.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you are facing large razors, and then finer ones, and keep doing this until it is done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the other delicate haircutting and breakage procedures, you should adjust your approach according to their orientation; this is something that cannot be adequately addressed by someone who has devoted themselves to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the affected area is exposed, it should be covered with one or more linen cloths according to the size of the wound, and then treated with oil, poured over the injury.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take one or two linen cloths that are doubled over, and soak them in wine and oil, then place them on the first linen cloth; do this as gently as possible so as not to burden the affected area. Then apply another bandage above, without pulling it too tightly, just enough to moisten the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	Leave it like this for one or two days until the abscess has subsided. Then remove the bandage and administer remedies such as thyme roots, flour of myrrh, incense powder, and similar substances; from these prepare a powder, apply it to the wound, then continue with further medications without causing irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure that the wound is clean immediately, do not leave any pus, nor allow it to coagulate in the bowe, for when pus assembles at the site of the brain's meshwork, it will flow and spread, causing great harm to the patient; because if you place something sharp on it, it will cut through from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that no accidents befall the patient, as we have said, where there is doubt, let it not cause fear.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if fear only comes from the medicine that has been applied, should it have this effect, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, and one spoonful in a spoon, and place it on the affected area;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then follows the treatment of various methods for healing until it is sound.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts above the nose are ever broken, or only one by itself, as these are two bones; and here below is cartilaginous tissue, which does not break, nor can it be bent or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must bend your little finger or ring finger at the nose, and place the break evenly inside your index finger, and through the tip outward, until the nose revives according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the area above the nose and cannot reach the nostril opening, it must be that you place him level with the tip of a knife slightly thicker than that.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, redo the operation, and strive to restore it on the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the abscess has subsided and is dressed, then apply a poultice to the bridge of the nose made of linen strips, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another one from the other side, if the break is on that side too; and let them be as thick as they fill in the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And they say that every restorer should moisten the tents with butter and change them each day. I do not think it is correct, but they should be moistened during the preparation of an egg broth, and with powder from the mill; then leave the tent until the bone has hardened and the cartilage is tough.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And instead of tents one uses goose feathers or no feathers at all, and if you have a half-cooked egg spread around them, and let the wound be open, and blow on the patient's lungs; or do whatever you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose in such a way that you are working on them, then place a wad of moistened cerotta or cotton in olive oil or in a drop of eardrop.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	And if the pus does not come out, then apply a plaster from outside, made of sawdust flour and incense powder mixed with yolk oil. Then place it on light bandages, but do not bind them too tightly.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the fracture is small and broken into many pieces, if it can be extracted with suitable instruments for that, then cut along the crack, and clean out anything that sticks or gets stuck inside, and solder together, as long as you use plasters and ointments suitable for this task;
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound inside the nose, then heal with trepanation, and place pine needles until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	On the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is ruptured from within, and there's no wound outwardly visible, only the breakage is outwardly visible. It doesn't split into two parts externally, rather it fractures internally; one can detect this by gently assessing it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary: if the breakage occurs in the right part, you should push your index finger into the mouth towards the side. And if the breakage is in the left mandible, you should use your right hand's index finger to push from outside and gently apply pressure on the inside of the breakage, then move it outward with the other hand evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there is an internal fracture of the jaw in two parts, then it is necessary that you apply extension to both halves until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or a rupture, hold them with a thread of gold or silver or silk. Then place wax on the broken mandible and put two strips of cloth above it; and place one large candlestick well made, or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, above the cloth strip, and bind it as tight as you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, allow it to settle for three days, and then adjust what has become unfastened; apply plaster on top, mixing with powder from the mill with enough egg or flour of almond after removing the wax. And place wool lightly on top of the plaster. If the plaster hardens and the patient's position does not change, let it be until it heals; many times heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come out, apply what we have instructed repeatedly.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, reward nothing of the bone when it is removed; so skillful are the tools for extracting such substances that they suffice.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains nothing, if the wound is wide, apply two poultices suitable for it to hasten flesh growth until it is healed.
de la forcele	by the power
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forces break many times before, towards the shoulder, and the breaking happens in three ways: where it is broken and torn into two parts, and there are pieces, and it is the more light to restore; or there is breaking with an injury.

And the operations are when the breaking is with an injury, that you have two ministers, so one marks the shoulder where the force breaks; and the other extends to the neck towards the body part. de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement. de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The process of breaking the splint.

If there's difficulty, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such events occur, or if the removal is only done after three days or more, and the wound lies on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place under the shoulder one thick cloth full of equal wool, and watch each hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the stitches become soft; if there is difficulty due to medicine's virtue, and give it meat as we have placed before, in such a way that the meat should be at first subtle; and when it starts to recover, let it swell. And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be recovered within forty days altogether; and then one must remove and apply baths and medicines to the wound for its healing. And if the constriction looks bad and is congested, you must leave removing until three or four months.
de la brisure du bras	From the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones which are called the 'foscile' pair. One bone is small, and it covers the pocket; the other is large, and this one lies underneath towards the small head. Sometimes only the large foscile breaks or even both bones break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small fosciles are broken, restoration is light and healing; and when the large ones are broken, healing is poor, and more troublesome than if they were broken together. If only the small foscile breaks, then it suffices to gently extend it, making it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large foscile that breaks, you should strain it more forcefully; place one cushion under it and lift the elbow higher than the other, and position the small finger lower than the others. And ensure the patient holds their own hand in a crossed position with an additional cushion slightly above them to prevent discomfort. Then have two attendants extend your arm up to its joint with respect to your hand or at an inch below it, and another attendant at the same level on the other side. Lastly, adjust their positions so that the hands are parallel to each other according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant. Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if during the break into wounds, I have spoken about this in another chapter; take care of the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the beginning of the restoration there appears pus, apply this: take a piece of cloth dipped in a mixture made from rose oil and white beeswax, so that it is neither too hard nor too soft; then attach two pieces of cloth together carefully, until the pus has subsided. Afterward, remove the beeswax, and place on it the plaster made from powder ground by the mill with plenty of egg yolk, put in the splints, and ensure that the splint is set higher than the breakage point, and slightly wider than the others; and be aware that there should be seven or eight splints arranged in various positions: when the breakage is within an os, or between two, place it more over the breakage than elsewhere, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and ensure that the cloths covering the breakage are moist but not wet, and neither hard nor rough; and use threads made from linen, not too thick or too thin, as we have said. And treat the limb and the joints for several days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itchiness appearing on it, you should immerse the limb in hot water until that itch is relieved; and let the limb not be made to rest. And then begin tightening again, and when the tie is undone and bone is uncovered, and similar occurrences, properly adjust it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if care is taken so that no injuries can occur on the limb because it is too tightly bound, you should soften it a bit with a poultice, and let it rest like this for several days until the injuries heal, then tighten again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things we have said happen to the patient, or if the loosening lasts for up to twenty days. de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and in our fingers there are few injuries, and they only bend many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary for the patient to lie flat on his back and stretch out his hands in front of him equally; then place his hand on an extended surface and extend the broken fingers, putting them evenly together until they are properly aligned; and put the bandage and splints, if there are no abscesses, then he should place a splint according to the size of his hand; and wrap it up in one piece of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the injury is at the base of the fingers near the belly of the hand's sole, make a frame with linen and instruct the patient to press it onto their broken toe; then stretch out this long piece of linen, and place the splint in such a way that its length matches the width of the hand's sole, and tighten it as it should be tightened.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is outside, it must be that you place one splint above and another under at the foot, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind both completely within the hand, and seal off the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break occurs in any of the fingers at all, when it's a sprain, just apply evenly; and compress with the palm, and if you see that applying a small straight splint helps lift the sprain, and prevents movement; and if the break is on other fingers like in the index or one of the others, apply evenly, and bind with the healthy one which follows; or you bind all together until movement occurs, or place on a splint like when you wrap; take care in restoring and arranging each dressing separately, and treat those who come with it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken knee

It is necessary that you wrap around the wound. Use a bandage double thick in two or three layers, and discard any excess. Then bend the leg until the heel reaches the knee, and insert one long thread between the thigh and leg, underneath from the knee upwards, and guide the thread's tip through the loops above; then continue wrapping around the leg and thigh with the bandage, place a pin on top of the wound and another on the bone in the leg. Then place eight inches of silk fabric between the leg and thigh as padding to evenly distribute pressure, then begin to wrap in three or four turns around the wound. de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg are two bones, from which one is called by right "mistletoe" and the other is called "fossil"; and there occurs any injury or breakage as it happens to the arm, and for this reason the restoration process is the same as with the arm, identically, and the procedures are all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, then turn them forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. And if the thick bones are broken, then you will feel and see great pain; turn them downwards. And when you have completed your work, take two sticks of horse hair that will cover the leg on both sides and be as long as the leg from the knee to below.
