de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the natural bone is broken in a woman's body, if it makes her appear swollen, then lean her towards the backside of her spine, and hold her by the buttocks. Then fill the natural gap with cotton, also placing it as roughly half an inch thick; then let the woman stand up, lift her back gradually, after which have her jump with the cotton filling until it reaches the opening of nature, and return the bone along with her breath; and when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and once she has urinated, have her resume the process for seven days or a bit more: thus will the break be healed. If you see fit, take a goat bladder, tie it onto the knot with string, and stuff the entire bladder into nature; then blow forcefully through the string until the bladder is inflated internally; nature will return the break. Then fill it with cotton, leave her in this state for a few days, till she is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the hand is broken, or if it happens to a woman, you should restore it in this manner as we have described for the hip bone; and these breaks do not go unnoticed by those who apply their effort and use to them, and heed my book. For, break signifies more than just various positions of the right path of restoration: thus understand it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of a broken penis, take an oyster shell and fill it with the penis; then wrap it tightly with bandages, and leave it for three days or somewhat longer; it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with a wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or similar, that they are now treated with bleeding, so that the bleedings we have mentioned bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, you should reapply vitriol, or if you don't have anything else, then restart the process of healing at the same time or on that day, or in case there are no pus discharges.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there are no pus discharges, let the healing continue up to the next day, until the pus is reduced. And don't touch it on the third or fourth day either, for you would be causing harmful accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if you see bone broken out on the cheekbone exposed surface, it is necessary to place it gently with your hands, in a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not suitable to place evenly with your hands, you should use this iron tool that is made of metal, which has seven inches or six inches in length, and its width suits the size of the wound; for this, it's necessary for the molder to take three or four pieces, according to what they need for each treatment of broken bones; and make sure it's round but a bit thick so that it doesn't bend when you compress it on your limb during work, and be sharp in front and large at the middle forward part like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", because the curved bones should be placed on the top of the visible bone; and strike once until you regain your place, and they must be even against each other. And if the breakage is delicate, and the tools cannot well grasp the bone, then you must cover the tip of the bone as long as the tool can hold it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone back as we said before, if you have an instrument suitable for this purpose or like a scalpel or a surgeon's knife at your power; then cut that which is stuck in the hard part of the bone and small scales.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been returned and if there is great pain from the patient afterward, know that it's not in its natural place. If you make it to be in its proper place, then moisten with one part of a tincture of vinegar for two days, and especially if it has healed externally; do not put any ointment or other thing on the wound that would cause infection or corruption; and instead allow the healing process without causing disturbance. Once you have restored the bone, apply these measures and leave the wound open to air, covering it entirely according to its size, and take great care so that the wound is not disturbed by pressure; and many times people have done this incorrectly, resulting in either death or corrosion at some point; and let your efforts be gentle and firm compared to other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is small or large and you doubt that harmful events might occur there as we said before, and you find pain in the limb, then it's not suitable to apply these measures; but cover externally instead of them, with hard cloths, and bind them together. And when after one day or two days you see improvement in the wound, remove whatever you have put on with vinegar, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, like the ointment tetrafarmaçon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And you must dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limb should be positioned so that the bone comes into contact with a slight ease.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the days continue and it can't heal properly at its place, be aware that there are small bone fragments causing this issue, so it is necessary for you to work on the wound with tension, and remove all these broken parts that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if a fistula occurs at the site or any other form of corruption, it must be treated according to what was explained in his previous chapter. And when bone is broken and exposed within the limb, such as the bones of the wrist or shoulder, or others like major limbs' bones, do not try to heal it immediately because many times this leads to death; instead let it heal naturally by itself for about 20 days or 30 days, then treat the wound if possible; and if you cannot, leave it untreated.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The burns often come after the healing of the wound, especially when it's close to the joint. There is much to observe in the figure of the limb; and by chance, one cannot do the natural actions with the limbs.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take caution therefore when it comes to these fresh burns: if you administer any of the restrictive medicines such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, sycamore bark, carob, and similar others, do so either individually or in combination with each other. Mix them with stoptive wine or enough egg or oil; then apply them in poultices on the affected area and hold them tightly but don't remove them daily. Remove it only when the nodules are gone. Or you can place it under a well-made piece of plaster because the property of plaster is such that it clears all swellings above limbs. If the nodulation turns into hardness like stone, requiring extraction, do so after applying a dressing until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the member which becomes weak after the siege
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breaking of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens for many reasons: due to which it was bound too tight, and was not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and could not reach the member's necessities; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to excess movements, not in its time; or due to having little blood in his body, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment involves making the patient eat their medicine and make their body tender until the pus multiplies within them; then they provide baths and give them joy and rest. Then apply wax to the limb so that the wax attracts to the large pus, and rinse it frequently with warm water until the pus corresponds to the limb. And restore its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is bent after the injury.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and if the bone was broken apart, then the form of the member becomes ugly. Nonetheless, it does not lose its natural function: nor should one believe those who say that we must break the whole limb anew; many people have done this in our land; these operations are criticized, and lead to great harms, even death. Still, if the fractures and injuries are fresh, then they should be soothed with hot water or medicines that soften tissues such as leaves of vismalve, roots, and mallow flowers and similar things. Then apply a moistening plaster made in this way; or take greased figs, grind them with corn meal, and other remedies that diminish the heat, and make a moistening plaster from these substances. Alternatively, you may use well-prepared yarrow, mix it with fat from geese liver or oil of sesame, and apply this as a plaster. Or take greasy figs, grind them with bran, and similar medicines to decrease the heat, and prepare a moistening plaster using these ingredients.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And always rub the dislocation with wet hands continuously and for a long time. And administer movements to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is old and hardened, like bone, and requires being treated with metal tools, then up to the bone if it's necessary, you should make incisions delicately; and consider and apply study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing great pain and injury to the patient.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation happens to none, if it fits now to bring back without hesitation.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if you delay, they swell the limbs, and by chance one might try to return it at its original place; for this does not suit that you move them in their swollen state: many times brought about pus and other pains.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If this happens, have the patient see a surgeon, then let them stay until all the pus has subsided; afterwards immerse the limb in hot water and oil, then gently manipulate it, and treat each limb as their treatment would occur naturally in its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters on shoulder dislocations up to this point.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	It happens that the jaws are dislocated downward, and the dislocations of both jaws occur in two ways: either they are somewhat ossified at their locations, and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the feet, causing saliva from the mouth to spill out, unable to hold it, nor close his mouth, and wrap his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it's whole and completed, you should reset it quickly without hesitation;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the ministers cut on the chief of the patient, and they push one of their fingers into the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth; if the dislocation is from 2 parts; and the other hand should be outside, to keep it even; and command the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers should remain evenly placed, until they reattach in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if they return to be sore, just as when the two jaws are together, should you use hot water and oil, so long as lightly moving them; do not overly force their movement back in place, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the disease closes well to be softened, then place wet cloths as wads in a poultice made from rose oil and beeswax, then bind it lightly with moist threads;
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the disease rest on its back, and keep its head between two cushions, so that it does not move to either side or strain itself, but please have light food given until the pains subside, and secure the jaws.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then let him chew lightly, and does not struggle with opening the mouth for eating and drinking, until the mandible is well set and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be correctly placed within an hour and are not turning back to their original position, it leads to fevers and habitual swelling, and sometimes stomach upset, and occasionally vomiting of pure liquid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, it has caused death in eight days for the one who experienced it.
de la forcelle	from the forcible act or action
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forces cannot relieve from within the middle of the ribcage and down to the backside; it is dislocated only once outward, and one feels this well indeed.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is such that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; then press onto the back as if with your palm, and it will return; then place them on the platter and cover with a cloth, and support them;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the shoulder that is toward the knife cannot be reset; if not, and if it is reset only once, then you must set it back to its place as we have said; then place them on the platter and with the bolster, and support them, and instruct the patient to rest until they are sane.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, the shoulder of the back is returned when it has been removed from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: of which one is that it dislocates at the part of the elbow towards the back; and the second is at the part below the knee; and by chance dislocates at the part above, and this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And it does not dislocate behind in the shoulder, nor inside through the nerves; and many times dislocates from below towards the elbow, especially for those who have little flesh, because with these jumps happens quickly; for those who have enough flesh, it jumps to points, and returns to points.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men a blow or fracture, and inflames the shoulder with an abscess, and fears that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must experiment on it as long as you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And once recognized the dislocation when it is pushed towards the shoulder blade, and you'll notice a clear distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their obvious diversity among them;
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a hollow at the shoulder blade's head, and from the shoulder to the neck, as if it were an eye; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move it with any motions;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And similarly, if it is dislocated upwards but not hidden, because you find it clearly at the neck;
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	In this manner of dislocation, it can only be corrected when it is new or if the child is small.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is for the ministers to lift their hand from the malady above, then place their hands on the shoulder blade, and lift the joint up strongly towards its natural position; and the ministers lift their hand, extend it upwards, then put it beneath; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the attendant should apply soothing and relaxing treatments, such as decoction of fennel and fenugreek and marjoram in hot water, and it should be applied.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then cover the patient's back with a cloth, and place on the shoulder blade a pad of even thickness, neither too soft nor too hard. Then put the heel under the pad, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand towards the malady.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And there are other operations that require the surgeon to keep the patient's head still so it doesn't move downwards. The shoulder is now moving back into place naturally, and if you observe while doing this task in the way I describe:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And ensure the place is as spacious as possible than that of the patient's body; and have them facing towards their side, and push the shoulder down near to the ribcage, and lift up the ribcage, so that the back leans backwards into an 'A' shape, making sure the muscles hang downwards.
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And there are other operations that require pulling the hand towards the back of the body moving downwards towards the belly. And if the muscles are too light, place something heavy on them and let the dislocation return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And there is also another way to do this: and you should put .i. long stick in the ground, so that the shoulder is positioned as such as .i. pistol, and it shouldn't be too big or too round;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Then place over the wound, but with a cloth under it, and let the wound stay as long as the length of the stick; then extend your hand down from the other side in formation, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if she does not wish to return with all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take two forearms of strong ones and four large ribs, which have the head round so it can enter halfway onto the base, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie the stick where the stick is covered with cloth underneath, so that the stick does not bruise the wound, then place it on the base under the wound; and extend your arm along the stick from its length, and tie the support on the stick, and the arm at the hand's head, then place the arm on one of a pitchfork's prongs of as wide width, and keep your hands down, and leave the body hanging from another side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is like this, in any manner, if you need to place an equal wool stick on the shoulder socket, then put the plaster covered with powdered mill grinding on top of this, along with incense and egg yolk butter spread all over the shoulder and around it. Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee can be dislocated in three ways: to understand this, it is within and without, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.

de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never fully set and always partially dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of this are that the ankle swells, and tends forward to the part where it is dislocated:

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	regarding injuries and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When injury comes with dislocation, and one seeks to restore it, many times it occurs that the patient dies.
